	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of file formats</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Wikimedia list article</div>
<table class="box-Cleanup_reorganize plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox rewrite.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Ambox_rewrite.svg/40px-Ambox_rewrite.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Ambox_rewrite.svg/60px-Ambox_rewrite.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Ambox_rewrite.svg/80px-Ambox_rewrite.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="620" data-file-height="620" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>may be in need of reorganization to comply with Wikipedia's <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Layout" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Layout">layout guidelines</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit">editing the article</a> to make improvements to the overall structure.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2019</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable plainlinks">This is a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">dynamic list</a> and may never be able to satisfy particular standards for completeness. You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit">expanding it</a> with <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources">reliably sourced</a> entries.</div>
<p>This is a <b>list of file formats</b> used by <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computers</a>, organized by type. <a href="/wiki/Filename_extension" title="Filename extension">Filename extensions</a> are usually noted in parentheses if they differ from the <a href="/wiki/File_format" title="File format">file format</a> name or abbreviation. Many <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating systems</a> do not limit filenames to one extension shorter than 4 characters, as was common with some operating systems that supported the <a href="/wiki/File_Allocation_Table" title="File Allocation Table">File Allocation Table</a> (FAT) file system.  Examples of operating systems that do not impose this limit include <a href="/wiki/Unix-like" title="Unix-like">Unix-like</a> systems, and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> <a href="/wiki/Windows_NT" title="Windows NT">NT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows_95" title="Windows 95">95</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows_98" title="Windows 98">98</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Windows_Me" title="Windows Me">ME</a> which have no three character limit on extensions for <a href="/wiki/32-bit" class="mw-redirect" title="32-bit">32-bit</a> or <a href="/wiki/64-bit" class="mw-redirect" title="64-bit">64-bit</a> applications on <a href="/wiki/File_system" title="File system">file systems</a> other than pre-Windows 95 and Windows NT 3.5 versions of the FAT file system.  Some filenames are given extensions longer than three characters.  While MS-DOS and NT always see the final period in a filename as an extension, in UNIX-like systems, the final period doesn't necessarily mean the text afterward is the extension.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some file formats, such as <code>.txt</code> or <code>.text</code>, may be listed multiple times.
</p>

<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-81"><a href="#Partial_files"><span class="tocnumber">38.3</span> <span class="toctext">Partial files</span></a>

</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Archive_and_compressed">Archive and compressed</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Archive and compressed">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_archive_formats" title="List of archive formats">List of archive formats</a></div>
<ul><li>.?Q? – files that are compressed, often by the <a href="/wiki/SQ_(program)" title="SQ (program)">SQ program</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/7z_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="7z (file format)">7z</a> – 7-Zip compressed file</li>
<li>AAPKG – <a href="/w/index.php?title=ArchestrA_Object_Package&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ArchestrA Object Package (page does not exist)">ArchestrA IDE</a><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://filext.com/file-extension/AAPKG">Details</a></li>
<li>AAC – <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Audio_Coding" title="Advanced Audio Coding">Advanced Audio Coding</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ACE_(compression_file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="ACE (compression file format)">ace</a> – ACE compressed file</li>
<li>ALZ – <a href="/wiki/ALZip" title="ALZip">ALZip</a> compressed file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/APK_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="APK (file format)">APK</a> – Applications installable on <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a></li>
<li>APPX – Microsoft Application Package (.appx)</li>
<li>AT3 – Sony's UMD data compression</li>
<li>.bke – BackupEarth.com data compression</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ARC_(file_format)" title="ARC (file format)">ARC</a> – pre-Zip data compression</li>
<li>ARC - <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> U8 Archive (mostly Yaz0 compressed)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ARJ" title="ARJ">ARJ</a> – ARJ compressed file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SubStation_Alpha" title="SubStation Alpha">ASS (also SAS)</a> – a subtitles file created by <a href="/wiki/Aegisub" title="Aegisub">Aegisub</a>, a video typesetting application (also a <a href="/wiki/Halo_(series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Halo (series)">Halo</a> game engine file)</li>
<li>B – (B file) Similar to .a, but a little less compressed...</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=.ba_(archive_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title=".ba (archive format) (page does not exist)">BA</a> – Scifer Archive (.ba), Scifer External Archive Type</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=.big&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title=".big (page does not exist)">big</a> – Special file compression format used by Electronic Arts to compress the data for many of EA's games</li>
<li>BIN – compressed archive, can be read and used by CD-ROMs and Java, extractable by 7-zip and WINRAR</li>
<li>bjsn – Used to store The Escapists saves on Android.</li>
<li>BKF (.bkf) – Microsoft backup created by <a href="/wiki/NTBackup" title="NTBackup">NTBackup</a>.c</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bzip2" title="Bzip2">bzip2</a> (.bz2) –</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Skyscraper_Sim_building&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Skyscraper Sim building (page does not exist)">bld</a> – Skyscraper Simulator Building</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(file_format)" title="Cabinet (file format)">cab</a> – A cabinet (.cab) file is a library of compressed files stored as one file. Cabinet files are used to organize installation files that are copied to the user's system.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>c4 – <a href="/wiki/JEDMICS" title="JEDMICS">JEDMICS</a> image files, a DOD system</li>
<li>cals – <a href="/wiki/JEDMICS" title="JEDMICS">JEDMICS</a> image files, a DOD system</li>
<li>CLIPFLAIR (.clipflair, .clipflair.zip) – ClipFlair Studio <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ClipFlair.net">ClipFlair</a> component saved state file (contains component options in XML, extra/attached files and nested components' state in child .clipflair.zip files – activities are also components and can be nested at any depth)</li>
<li>CPT, SEA – <a href="/wiki/Compact_Pro" title="Compact Pro">Compact Pro</a> (<a href="/wiki/Macintosh" title="Macintosh">Macintosh</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Direct_Access_Archive" title="Direct Access Archive">DAA</a> – Closed-format, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Windows</a>-only compressed disk image</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Deb_(file_format)" title="Deb (file format)">deb</a> – <a href="/wiki/Debian" title="Debian">Debian</a> install package</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/.dmg" class="mw-redirect" title=".dmg">DMG</a> – an Apple compressed/encrypted format</li>
<li>DDZ – a file which can only be used by the "daydreamer engine" created by "fever-dreamer", a program similar to RAGS, it's mainly used to make somewhat short games.</li>
<li>DN – Adobe Dimension CC file format</li>
<li>DPE – Package of AVE documents made with <a href="/wiki/Aquafadas" class="mw-redirect" title="Aquafadas">Aquafadas</a> digital publishing tools.</li>
<li>.egg – Alzip Egg Edition compressed file</li>
<li>EGT (.egt) – EGT Universal Document also used to create compressed cabinet files replaces .ecab</li>
<li>ECAB (.ECAB, .ezip) – EGT Compressed Folder used in advanced systems to compress entire system folders, replaced by EGT Universal Document</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Electronic_software_distribution" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronic software distribution">ESD</a> – Electronic Software Distribution, a <a href="/wiki/Data_compression" title="Data compression">compressed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Encrypted" class="mw-redirect" title="Encrypted">encrypted</a> WIM File</li>
<li>ESS (.ess) – EGT SmartSense File, detects files compressed using the EGT compression system.</li>
<li>Flipchart file (.flipchart) – Used in <a href="/wiki/Promethean_World" title="Promethean World">Promethean</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://support.prometheanworld.com/product/activinspire">ActivInspire</a> Flipchart Software.</li>
<li>GBP – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://fileinfo.com/extension/gbp">GBP File Extension – What is a .gbp file and how do I open it?</a> 2 types of files: 1. An <b>archive index file</b> that is created by Genie Timeline <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.genie9.com/Home/Genie_Timeline_Home/overview.aspx">[3]</a>. It contains references to the files that the user has chosen to backup; the references can be to an archive file or a batch of files. This files can be opened using Genie-Soft Genie Timeline on Windows. 2. A <b>data output file</b> created by CAD Printed Circuit Board (PCB). This type of file can be opened on Windows using Autodesk EAGLE <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.autodesk.com/products/eagle/overview">EAGLE | PCB Design Software | Autodesk</a>, Altium Designer <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://products.live.altium.com/">[4]</a>, Viewplot <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.viewplot.com/">Welcome to Viewplot.com ...For PCB Related Software;...Viewplot The Gerber Viewer &amp; editor in one......PCB Elegance a professional layout package for a affordable price</a>, Gerbv <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://gerbv.geda-project.org/">gerbv – A Free/Open Source Gerber Viewer</a> on Mac using Autodesk EAGLE, Gerbv, gEDA <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.gpleda.org/index.html">gplEDA Homepage</a> and on Linux using Autodesk EAGLE, gEDA, Gerbv</li>
<li>GHO (.gho, .ghs) – <a href="/wiki/Norton_Ghost" class="mw-redirect" title="Norton Ghost">Norton Ghost</a></li>
<li>GIF (.gif) – Graphics Interchange Format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gzip" title="Gzip">gzip</a> (.gz) – Compressed file</li>
<li>HTML (.html) HTML code file</li>
<li>IPG (.ipg) – Format in which <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a> packages their <a href="/wiki/IPod_game" title="IPod game">iPod games</a>. can be extracted through <a href="/wiki/Winrar" class="mw-redirect" title="Winrar">Winrar</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jar_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jar (file format)">jar</a> – ZIP file with manifest for use with <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a> applications.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lawrence_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lawrence (file format) (page does not exist)">LBR</a> (.Lawrence) – Lawrence Compiler Type file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LBR_(file_format)" title="LBR (file format)">LBR</a> – Library file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LBR_(file_format)" title="LBR (file format)">LQR</a> – LBR Library file compressed by the <a href="/wiki/SQ_(program)" title="SQ (program)">SQ program</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LHA_(file_format)" title="LHA (file format)">LHA</a> (.lzh) – Lempel, Ziv, Huffman</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lzip" title="Lzip">lzip</a> (.lz) – Compressed file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lzo" class="mw-redirect" title="Lzo">lzo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lempel%E2%80%93Ziv%E2%80%93Markov_chain_algorithm" title="Lempel–Ziv–Markov chain algorithm">lzma</a> – Lempel–Ziv–Markov chain algorithm compressed file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LZX" title="LZX">LZX</a></li>
<li>MBW (.mbw) – <a href="/wiki/MBRWizard" class="mw-redirect" title="MBRWizard">MBRWizard</a> archive</li>
<li>MHTML – Mine HTML (Hyper-Text Markup Language) code file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MPQ_(file_format)" title="MPQ (file format)">MPQ</a> Archives (.mpq) – Used by <a href="/wiki/Blizzard_Entertainment" title="Blizzard Entertainment">Blizzard Entertainment</a></li>
<li>BIN (.bin) – <a href="/wiki/MacBinary" title="MacBinary">MacBinary</a></li>
<li>NTH (.nth) – Nokia Theme Used by <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a> <a href="/wiki/Series_40" title="Series 40">Series 40</a> Cellphones</li>
<li>OAR (.oar) – OmegaARc Archive</li>
<li>OSZ – <a href="/wiki/Osu!" title="Osu!">osu!</a> compressed beatmap archive</li>
<li>PAK – Enhanced type of .ARC archive</li>
<li>PAR (.par, .par2) – <a href="/wiki/Parchive" title="Parchive">Parchive</a></li>
<li>PAF (.paf) – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portable_Application_File&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Portable Application File (page does not exist)">Portable Application File</a></li>
<li>PEA (.pea) – PeaZip archive file</li>
<li>PHP (.php) – PHP code file</li>
<li>PYK (.pyk) – Compressed file</li>
<li>PK3 (.pk3) – <a href="/wiki/Quake_3" class="mw-redirect" title="Quake 3">Quake 3</a> archive (See note on Doom³)</li>
<li>PK4 (.pk4) – <a href="/wiki/Doom%C2%B3" class="mw-redirect" title="Doom³">Doom³</a> archive (Opens similarly to a <a href="/wiki/ZIP_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="ZIP (file format)">zip</a> archive.)</li>
<li>py / pyw – Python code file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/RAR_(file_format)" title="RAR (file format)">RAR</a> (.rar) – Rar Archive, for multiple file archive (rar to .r01-.r99 to s01 and so on)</li>
<li>RAG, RAGS – Game file, a game playable in the RAGS game-engine, a free program which both allows people to create games, and play games, games created have the format "RAG game file"</li>
<li>RaX – Archive file created by RaX</li>
<li>RPM – <a href="/wiki/Red_Hat_Package_Manager" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Hat Package Manager">Red Hat</a> package/installer for Fedora, RHEL, and similar systems.</li>
<li>sb – Scratch file</li>
<li>sb2 – Scratch 2.0 file</li>
<li>sb3 - Scratch 3.0 file</li>
<li>SEN – Scifer Archive (.sen) – Scifer Internal Archive Type</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/StuffIt" title="StuffIt">SIT</a> (.sitx) – StuffIt (<a href="/wiki/Macintosh" title="Macintosh">Macintosh</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SIS_(file_format)" title="SIS (file format)">SIS</a>/<a href="/wiki/SISX" class="mw-redirect" title="SISX">SISX</a> – <a href="/wiki/Symbian" title="Symbian">Symbian</a> Application Package</li>
<li>SKB – Google <a href="/wiki/SketchUp" title="SketchUp">SketchUp</a> backup File</li>
<li>SQ (.sq) – Squish Compressed Archive</li>
<li>SWM – Splitted WIM File, usually found on <a href="/wiki/OEM" class="mw-redirect" title="OEM">OEM</a> <a href="/wiki/WinRE" class="mw-redirect" title="WinRE">Recovery Partition</a> to store preinstalled Windows image, and to make Recovery backup (to USB Drive) easier (due to FAT32 limitations)</li>
<li>SZS – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> Yaz0 Compressed Archive</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tar_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tar (file format)">TAR</a> – group of files, packaged as one file</li>
<li>TGZ (<a href="/wiki/Gzip" title="Gzip">.tar.gz</a>) – gzipped tar file</li>
<li>TB (.tb) – Tabbery Virtual Desktop Tab file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TIB_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="TIB (file format)">TIB</a> (.tib) – <a href="/wiki/Acronis_True_Image" title="Acronis True Image">Acronis True Image</a> backup</li>
<li>UHA – Ultra High Archive Compression</li>
<li>UUE (.uue) – unified utility engine – the generic and default format for all things UUe-related.</li>
<li>VIV – Archive format used to compress data for several video games, including <a href="/wiki/Need_For_Speed:_High_Stakes" class="mw-redirect" title="Need For Speed: High Stakes">Need For Speed: High Stakes</a>.</li>
<li>VOL – video game data package.</li>
<li>VSA – <a href="/wiki/Altiris" title="Altiris">Altiris</a> Virtual Software Archive</li>
<li>WAX – Wavexpress – A ZIP alternative optimized for packages containing video, allowing multiple packaged files to be all-or-none delivered with near-instantaneous unpacking via NTFS file system manipulation.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Windows_Imaging_Format" title="Windows Imaging Format">WIM</a> – A compressed disk image for installing <a href="/wiki/Windows_Vista" title="Windows Vista">Windows Vista</a> or higher, <a href="/wiki/Windows_Fundamentals_for_Legacy_PC" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows Fundamentals for Legacy PC">Windows Fundamentals for Legacy PC</a>, or restoring a system image made from Backup and Restore (<a href="/wiki/Windows_Vista" title="Windows Vista">Windows Vista</a>/<a href="/wiki/Windows_7" title="Windows 7">7</a>)</li>
<li>XAP – <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">Windows Phone</a> Application Package</li>
<li>xz – xz compressed files, based on <a href="/wiki/Lempel%E2%80%93Ziv%E2%80%93Markov_chain_algorithm" title="Lempel–Ziv–Markov chain algorithm">LZMA/LZMA2</a> algorithm</li>
<li>Z – <a href="/wiki/Unix" title="Unix">Unix</a> <a href="/wiki/Compress" title="Compress">compress</a> file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zoo_(file_format)" title="Zoo (file format)">zoo</a> – based on <a href="/wiki/LZW" class="mw-redirect" title="LZW">LZW</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ZIP_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="ZIP (file format)">zip</a> – popular compression format</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_recordable_media_archiving">Physical recordable media archiving</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Physical recordable media archiving">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/ISO_image" title="ISO image">ISO</a> – The generic format for most optical media, including <a href="/wiki/CD-ROM" title="CD-ROM">CD-ROM</a>, <a href="/wiki/DVD-ROM" class="mw-redirect" title="DVD-ROM">DVD-ROM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" class="mw-redirect" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a>, <a href="/wiki/HD_DVD" title="HD DVD">HD DVD</a> and <a href="/wiki/Universal_Media_Disc" title="Universal Media Disc">UMD</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NRG_(file_format)" title="NRG (file format)">NRG</a> – The proprietary optical media archive format used by <a href="/wiki/Nero_AG" title="Nero AG">Nero</a> applications.</li>
<li>IMG – For archiving <a href="/wiki/DOS" title="DOS">DOS</a> formatted <a href="/wiki/Floppy_disks" class="mw-redirect" title="Floppy disks">floppy disks</a>, larger optical media, and hard disk drives.</li>
<li>ADF – <i><a href="/wiki/Amiga_Disk_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Amiga Disk Format">Amiga Disk Format</a></i>, for archiving <a href="/wiki/Amiga" title="Amiga">Amiga</a> floppy disks
<ul><li>ADZ – The GZip-compressed version of ADF.</li>
<li>DMS – <i><a href="/wiki/Disk_Masher_System" title="Disk Masher System">Disk Masher System</a></i>, a disk-archiving system native to the Amiga.</li></ul></li>
<li>DSK – For archiving floppy disks from a number of other platforms, including the <a href="/wiki/ZX_Spectrum" title="ZX Spectrum">ZX&#160;Spectrum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amstrad_CPC" title="Amstrad CPC">Amstrad CPC</a>.</li>
<li>D64 – An archive of a <a href="/wiki/Commodore_64" title="Commodore 64">Commodore 64</a> floppy disk.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/System_Deployment_Image" title="System Deployment Image">SDI</a> – System Deployment Image, used for archiving and providing "virtual disk" functionality.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MDS_file" class="mw-redirect" title="MDS file">MDS</a> – <a href="/wiki/DAEMON_tools" class="mw-redirect" title="DAEMON tools">DAEMON tools</a> native disc image format used for making images from optical <a href="/wiki/CD-ROM" title="CD-ROM">CD-ROM</a>, <a href="/wiki/DVD-ROM" class="mw-redirect" title="DVD-ROM">DVD-ROM</a>, <a href="/wiki/HD_DVD" title="HD DVD">HD DVD</a> or <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" class="mw-redirect" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a>. It comes together with MDF file and can be mounted with DAEMON Tools.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MDX_file" class="mw-redirect" title="MDX file">MDX</a> – New <a href="/wiki/DAEMON_Tools" class="mw-redirect" title="DAEMON Tools">DAEMON Tools</a> format that allows getting one MDX disc image file instead of two (MDF and MDS).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Apple_Disk_Image" title="Apple Disk Image">DMG</a> – Macintosh disk image files</li></ul>
<p>(MPEG-1 is found in a .DAT file on a video CD.)
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/DiscJuggler" title="DiscJuggler">CDI</a> – DiscJuggler image file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CDRWin" class="mw-redirect" title="CDRWin">CUE</a> – CDRWrite CUE image file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Easy_CD_Creator" class="mw-redirect" title="Easy CD Creator">CIF</a> – Easy CD Creator .cif format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Roxio_Creator" title="Roxio Creator">C2D</a> – Roxio-WinOnCD .c2d format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Direct_Access_Archive" title="Direct Access Archive">DAA</a> – PowerISO .daa format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BlindWrite" title="BlindWrite">B6T</a> – BlindWrite 5/6 image file</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ceramics_glaze_recipes">Ceramics glaze recipes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ceramics glaze recipes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>File formats for software, databases, and websites used by potters and ceramic artists to manage glaze recipes, glaze chemistry, etc.
</p>
<ul><li>GlazeChem text format <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://insight-live.com/insight/">INSIGHT Live, OnLine INSIGHT</a></li>
<li>GlazeMaster .tab xml (GlazeMaster software)<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.masteringglazes.com/glazemaster/">GlazeMaster™ | Welcome to masteringglazes.com | John Hesselberth</a><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160507162807/https://ceramicrecipes.org/ceramic-recipes-faq">Ceramic Recipes FAQ | Ceramic Recipes</a><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://insight-live.com/insight/">INSIGHT Live, OnLine INSIGHT</a></li>
<li>HyperGlaze .hgz (HyperGlaze software) <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.hyperglaze.com">HyperGlaze – glaze software for artists</a><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160507162807/https://ceramicrecipes.org/ceramic-recipes-faq">[5]</a><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://insight-live.com/insight/">INSIGHT Live, OnLine INSIGHT</a></li>
<li>Insight .xml (DigitalFire Insight software)<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20180117011830/https://www.digitalfire.com/insight/index.php">Wayback Machine</a><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20180117011957/https://www.digitalfire.com/insightfaq.php#faqMiscellaneous">[6]</a></li>
<li>Insight .rcp (deprecated, DigitalFire Insight software)<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20180117011957/https://www.digitalfire.com/insightfaq.php#faqMiscellaneous">Wayback Machine</a></li>
<li>Insight .rcx (deprecated, DigitalFire Insight software)<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20180117011957/https://www.digitalfire.com/insightfaq.php#faqMiscellaneous">Wayback Machine</a></li>
<li>Matrix <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.matrix2000.co.nz">Matrix Glaze Software</a><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://insight-live.com/insight/">INSIGHT Live, OnLine INSIGHT</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Computer-aided_design">Computer-aided design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Computer-aided design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Computer-aided" title="Computer-aided">Computer-aided</a> is a prefix for several categories of tools (e.g., design, manufacture, engineering) which assist professionals in their respective fields (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Machining" title="Machining">machining</a>, <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schematics" class="mw-redirect" title="Schematics">schematics</a>).
</p>
<h3><span id="Computer-aided_design_.28CAD.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Computer-aided_design_(CAD)">Computer-aided design (CAD)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Computer-aided design (CAD)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Computer-aided_design" title="Computer-aided design">Computer-aided design</a> (CAD) software assists engineers, architects and other design professionals in project design.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/3DXML" title="3DXML">3DXML</a> – Dassault Systemes graphic representation</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/3D_Manufacturing_Format" title="3D Manufacturing Format">3MF</a> – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> 3D Manufacturing Format<sup id="cite_ref-msdn.microsoft.com_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msdn.microsoft.com-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>ACP – VA Software <a href="/w/index.php?title=VA_%E2%80%93_Virtual_Architecture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="VA – Virtual Architecture (page does not exist)">VA – Virtual Architecture</a> CAD file</li>
<li>AMF – <a href="/wiki/Additive_Manufacturing_File_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Additive Manufacturing File Format">Additive Manufacturing File Format</a></li>
<li>AEC – DataCAD drawing format<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>AR – Ashlar-Vellum Argon – 3D Modeling</li>
<li>ART – ArtCAM model</li>
<li>ASC – <a href="/wiki/BRL-CAD" title="BRL-CAD">BRL-CAD</a> Geometry File (old ASCII format)</li>
<li>ASM – Solidedge Assembly, Pro/ENGINEER Assembly</li>
<li>BIN, BIM – <a href="/wiki/Data_Design_System" title="Data Design System">Data Design System</a> DDS-CAD</li>
<li>BREP – <a href="/wiki/Open_CASCADE" class="mw-redirect" title="Open CASCADE">Open CASCADE</a> 3D model (shape)</li>
<li>C3D – <a href="/wiki/C3D_Toolkit" title="C3D Toolkit">C3D Toolkit</a> File Format</li>
<li>CCC – CopyCAD Curves</li>
<li>CCM – CopyCAD Model</li>
<li>CCS – CopyCAD Session</li>
<li>CAD – CadStd</li>
<li>CATDrawing – <a href="/wiki/CATIA" title="CATIA">CATIA</a> V5 Drawing document</li>
<li>CATPart – <a href="/wiki/CATIA" title="CATIA">CATIA</a> V5 Part document</li>
<li>CATProduct – <a href="/wiki/CATIA" title="CATIA">CATIA</a> V5 Assembly document</li>
<li>CATProcess – <a href="/wiki/CATIA" title="CATIA">CATIA</a> V5 Manufacturing document</li>
<li>cgr – <a href="/wiki/CATIA" title="CATIA">CATIA</a> V5 graphic representation file</li>
<li>ckd – <a href="/wiki/KeyCreator" title="KeyCreator">KeyCreator</a> CAD Modeling</li>
<li>ckt – <a href="/wiki/KeyCreator" title="KeyCreator">KeyCreator</a> CAD Modeling</li>
<li>CO – Ashlar-Vellum Cobalt – parametric drafting and 3D modeling</li>
<li>DRW – <a href="/wiki/Caddie_(CAD_system)" title="Caddie (CAD system)">Caddie</a> Early version of Caddie drawing – Prior to Caddie changing to DWG</li>
<li>DFT – Solidedge Draft</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DGN" title="DGN">DGN</a> – <a href="/wiki/MicroStation" title="MicroStation">MicroStation</a> design file</li>
<li>DGK – Delcam Geometry</li>
<li>DMT – Delcam Machining Triangles</li>
<li>DXF – <a href="/wiki/ASCII_Drawing_Interchange_file_format" class="mw-redirect" title="ASCII Drawing Interchange file format">ASCII Drawing Interchange file format</a>, <a href="/wiki/AutoCAD" title="AutoCAD">AutoCAD</a></li>
<li>DWB – <a href="/wiki/VariCAD" title="VariCAD">VariCAD</a> drawing file</li>
<li>DWF – Autodesk's Web Design Format; AutoCAD &amp; <a href="/wiki/Autodesk_Revit" title="Autodesk Revit">Revit</a> can publish to this format; similar in concept to PDF files; Autodesk Design Review is the reader</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/.dwg" title=".dwg">DWG</a> – Popular file format for Computer Aided Drafting applications, notably <a href="/wiki/AutoCAD" title="AutoCAD">AutoCAD</a>, Open Design Alliance applications, and <a href="/wiki/Autodesk_Inventor" title="Autodesk Inventor">Autodesk Inventor</a> Drawing files</li>
<li>EASM – SolidWorks eDrawings assembly file</li>
<li>EDRW – eDrawings drawing file</li>
<li>EMB – Wilcom ES Designer Embroidery CAD file</li>
<li>EPRT – eDrawings part file</li>
<li>EscPcb – "esCAD pcb" data file by <a href="/wiki/Electro-System" title="Electro-System">Electro-System</a> (Japan)</li>
<li>EscSch – "esCAD sch" data file by <a href="/wiki/Electro-System" title="Electro-System">Electro-System</a> (Japan)</li>
<li>ESW – AGTEK format</li>
<li>EXCELLON – <a href="/wiki/Excellon_file" class="mw-redirect" title="Excellon file">Excellon file</a></li>
<li>EXP – <a href="/wiki/Drawing_Express" title="Drawing Express">Drawing Express</a> format</li>
<li>F3D – Autodesk Fusion 360 archive file<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>FCStd – Native file format of <a href="/wiki/FreeCAD" title="FreeCAD">FreeCAD</a> <a href="/wiki/CAD" class="mw-redirect" title="CAD">CAD</a>/<a href="/wiki/Computer-aided_manufacturing" title="Computer-aided manufacturing">CAM</a> package</li>
<li>FM – FeatureCAM Part File</li>
<li>FMZ – FormZ Project file</li>
<li>G – <a href="/wiki/BRL-CAD" title="BRL-CAD">BRL-CAD</a> Geometry File</li>
<li>GBR – <a href="/wiki/Gerber_file" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerber file">Gerber file</a></li>
<li>GLM – <a href="/wiki/KernelCAD" title="KernelCAD">KernelCAD</a> model</li>
<li>GRB – <a href="/wiki/T-FLEX_CAD" title="T-FLEX CAD">T-FLEX CAD</a> File</li>
<li>GTC – <a href="/wiki/GRAITEC_Advance" title="GRAITEC Advance">GRAITEC Advance</a> format</li>
<li>IAM – <a href="/wiki/Autodesk_Inventor" title="Autodesk Inventor">Autodesk Inventor</a> Assembly file</li>
<li>ICD – IronCAD 2D CAD file</li>
<li>IDW – <a href="/wiki/Autodesk_Inventor" title="Autodesk Inventor">Autodesk Inventor</a> Drawing file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Industry_Foundation_Classes" title="Industry Foundation Classes">IFC</a> – <a href="/wiki/BuildingSMART" title="BuildingSMART">buildingSMART</a> for sharing AEC and <a href="/wiki/Facility_management" title="Facility management">FM</a> data</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/IGES" title="IGES">IGES</a> – Initial Graphics Exchange Specification</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Intergraph_Standard_File_Formats" title="Intergraph Standard File Formats">Intergraph Standard File Formats</a> – <a href="/wiki/Intergraph" title="Intergraph">Intergraph</a></li>
<li>IPN – <a href="/wiki/Autodesk_Inventor" title="Autodesk Inventor">Autodesk Inventor</a> Presentation file</li>
<li>IPT – <a href="/wiki/Autodesk_Inventor" title="Autodesk Inventor">Autodesk Inventor</a> Part file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JT_(visualization_format)" title="JT (visualization format)">JT</a> – Jupiter Tesselation</li>
<li>MCD – Monu-CAD (Monument/Headstone Drawing file)</li>
<li>model – <a href="/wiki/CATIA" title="CATIA">CATIA</a> V4 part document</li>
<li>OCD – <a href="/wiki/Orienteering" title="Orienteering">Orienteering</a> Computer Aided Design (OCAD) file</li>
<li>PAR – Solidedge Part</li>
<li>PIPE – PIPE-FLO Professional Piping system design file</li>
<li>PLN – ArchiCad project</li>
<li>PRT – NX (recently known as Unigraphics), Pro/ENGINEER Part, CADKEY Part</li>
<li>PSM – Solidedge Sheet</li>
<li>PSMODEL – PowerSHAPE Model</li>
<li>PWI – PowerINSPECT File</li>
<li>PYT – Pythagoras File</li>
<li>SKP – SketchUp Model</li>
<li>RLF – ArtCAM Relief</li>
<li>RVM – <a href="/wiki/AVEVA" class="mw-redirect" title="AVEVA">AVEVA</a> <a href="/wiki/PDMS_(software)" title="PDMS (software)">PDMS</a> 3D Review model</li>
<li>RVT – <a href="/wiki/Autodesk_Revit" title="Autodesk Revit">Autodesk Revit</a> project files</li>
<li>RFA – <a href="/wiki/Autodesk_Revit" title="Autodesk Revit">Autodesk Revit</a> family files</li>
<li>S12 – Spirit file, by Softtech</li>
<li>SCAD – <a href="/wiki/OpenSCAD" title="OpenSCAD">OpenSCAD</a> 3D part model</li>
<li>SCDOC – <a href="/wiki/SpaceClaim" title="SpaceClaim">SpaceClaim</a> 3D Part/Assembly</li>
<li>SLDASM – <a href="/wiki/SolidWorks" title="SolidWorks">SolidWorks</a> Assembly drawing</li>
<li>SLDDRW – <a href="/wiki/SolidWorks" title="SolidWorks">SolidWorks</a> 2D drawing</li>
<li>SLDPRT – <a href="/wiki/SolidWorks" title="SolidWorks">SolidWorks</a> 3D part model</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DotXSI" title="DotXSI">dotXSI</a> – For <a href="/wiki/Softimage" class="mw-redirect" title="Softimage">Softimage</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Standard_for_the_Exchange_of_Product_model_data" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard for the Exchange of Product model data">STEP</a> – Standard for the Exchange of Product model data</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/STL_(file_format)" title="STL (file format)">STL</a> – Stereo Lithographic data format used by various CAD systems and stereo lithographic printing machines.</li>
<li>STD – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Power_Vision_Plus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Power Vision Plus (page does not exist)">Power Vision Plus</a> – Electricity Meter Data (Circutor)</li>
<li>TCT – <a href="/wiki/TurboCAD" title="TurboCAD">TurboCAD</a> drawing template</li>
<li>TCW – <a href="/wiki/TurboCAD" title="TurboCAD">TurboCAD</a> for Windows 2D and 3D drawing</li>
<li>UNV – <a href="/wiki/I-DEAS" title="I-DEAS">I-DEAS</a> I-DEAS (Integrated Design and Engineering Analysis Software)</li>
<li>VC6 – Ashlar-Vellum Graphite – 2D and 3D drafting</li>
<li>VLM – Ashlar-Vellum Vellum, Vellum 2D, Vellum Draft, Vellum 3D, DrawingBoard</li>
<li>VS – Ashlar-Vellum Vellum Solids</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/VRML#WRL_File_Format" title="VRML">WRL</a> – Similar to STL, but includes color. Used by various CAD systems and 3D printing rapid prototyping machines. Also used for VRML models on the web.</li>
<li>X_B – <a href="/wiki/Parasolid" title="Parasolid">Parasolids</a> binary format</li>
<li>X_T – <a href="/wiki/Parasolid" title="Parasolid">Parasolids</a></li>
<li>XE – Ashlar-Vellum Xenon – for associative 3D modeling</li>
<li>ZOFZPROJ – ZofzPCB 3D PCB model, containing mesh, netlist and BOM</li></ul>
<h3><span id="Electronic_design_automation_.28EDA.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Electronic_design_automation_(EDA)">Electronic design automation (EDA)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Electronic design automation (EDA)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Electronic_design_automation" title="Electronic design automation">Electronic design automation</a> (EDA), or electronic computer-aided design (ECAD), is specific to the field of electrical engineering.
</p>
<ul><li>BRD – Board file for <a href="/wiki/EAGLE_(program)" title="EAGLE (program)">EAGLE Layout Editor</a>, a commercial <a href="/wiki/Printed_circuit_board" title="Printed circuit board">PCB</a> design tool</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Boundary_scan_description_language" title="Boundary scan description language">BSDL</a> – Description language for testing through <a href="/wiki/Joint_Test_Action_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Joint Test Action Group">JTAG</a></li>
<li>CDL – <a href="/wiki/Transistor" title="Transistor">Transistor</a>-level <a href="/wiki/Netlist" title="Netlist">netlist</a> format for <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">IC</a> design</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Common_Power_Format" title="Common Power Format">CPF</a> – Power-domain specification in <a href="/wiki/System-on-a-chip" class="mw-redirect" title="System-on-a-chip">system-on-a-chip</a> (SoC) implementation (see also <a href="/wiki/Unified_Power_Format" title="Unified Power Format">UPF</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Design_Exchange_Format" title="Design Exchange Format">DEF</a> – <a href="/wiki/Logic_gate" title="Logic gate">Gate</a>-level <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit_layout" title="Integrated circuit layout">layout</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Detailed_Standard_Parasitic_Format&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Detailed Standard Parasitic Format (page does not exist)">DSPF</a> – Detailed Standard Parasitic Format, <a href="/wiki/Analog_signal" title="Analog signal">Analog</a>-level <a href="/w/index.php?title=Parasitic_component&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Parasitic component (page does not exist)">parasitics</a> of interconnections in <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">IC</a> design</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/EDIF" title="EDIF">EDIF</a> – Vendor neutral <a href="/wiki/Logic_gate" title="Logic gate">gate</a>-level <a href="/wiki/Netlist" title="Netlist">netlist</a> format</li>
<li>FSDB – <a href="/wiki/Analog_signal" title="Analog signal">Analog</a> <a href="/wiki/Waveform" title="Waveform">waveform</a> format (see also <a href="/wiki/Waveform_viewer" title="Waveform viewer">Waveform viewer</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GDSII" title="GDSII">GDSII</a> – Format for <a href="/wiki/Printed_circuit_board" title="Printed circuit board">PCB</a> and <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit_layout" title="Integrated circuit layout">layout</a> of integrated circuits</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Intel_HEX" title="Intel HEX">HEX</a> – <a href="/wiki/ASCII" title="ASCII">ASCII</a>-coded <a href="/wiki/Binary_file" title="Binary file">binary</a> format for <a href="/wiki/Memory_dump" class="mw-redirect" title="Memory dump">memory dumps</a></li>
<li>LEF – Library Exchange Format, physical abstract of cells for <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">IC</a> design</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liberty_(EDA)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Liberty (EDA) (page does not exist)">LIB</a> – <a href="/wiki/Library_(electronics)#Library" class="mw-redirect" title="Library (electronics)">Library</a> modeling (<a href="/wiki/Logic_function" class="mw-redirect" title="Logic function">function</a>, timing) format</li>
<li>MS12 – <a href="/wiki/NI_Multisim" title="NI Multisim">NI Multisim</a> file</li>
<li>OASIS – <a href="/wiki/Open_Artwork_System_Interchange_Standard" title="Open Artwork System Interchange Standard">Open Artwork System Interchange Standard</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OpenAccess" title="OpenAccess">OpenAccess</a> – Design database format with <a href="/wiki/Application_Programming_Interface" class="mw-redirect" title="Application Programming Interface">APIs</a></li>
<li>PSF – Cadence proprietary format to store simulation results/waveforms (2GB limit)</li>
<li>PSFXL – Cadence proprietary format to store simulation results/waveforms</li>
<li>SDC – Synopsys Design Constraints, format for <a href="/wiki/Logic_synthesis" title="Logic synthesis">synthesis</a> constraints</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Standard_Delay_Format" title="Standard Delay Format">SDF</a> – Standard for <a href="/wiki/Logic_gate" title="Logic gate">gate</a>-level timings</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Standard_Parasitic_Exchange_Format" title="Standard Parasitic Exchange Format">SPEF</a> – Standard format for <a href="/w/index.php?title=Parasitic_component&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Parasitic component (page does not exist)">parasitics</a> of interconnections in <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">IC</a> design</li>
<li>SPI, CIR – <a href="/wiki/SPICE" title="SPICE">SPICE</a> Netlist, device-level <a href="/wiki/Netlist" title="Netlist">netlist</a> and commands for <a href="/wiki/Computer_simulation" title="Computer simulation">simulation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SREC_(file_format)" title="SREC (file format)">SREC</a>, S19 – S-record, <a href="/wiki/ASCII" title="ASCII">ASCII</a>-coded format for <a href="/wiki/Memory_dump" class="mw-redirect" title="Memory dump">memory dumps</a></li>
<li>SST2 – Cadence proprietary format to store mixed-signal simulation results/waveforms</li>
<li>STIL – Standard Test Interface Language, IEEE1450-1999 standard for Test Patterns for <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">IC</a></li>
<li>SV – <a href="/wiki/SystemVerilog" title="SystemVerilog">SystemVerilog</a> source file</li>
<li>S*P – <a href="/wiki/Touchstone_file" title="Touchstone file">Touchstone</a>/<a href="/wiki/EEsof" class="mw-redirect" title="EEsof">EEsof</a> Scattering parameter data file – multi-port blackbox performance, measurement or simulated</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Unified_Power_Format" title="Unified Power Format">UPF</a> – Standard for Power-domain specification in <a href="/wiki/System-on-a-chip" class="mw-redirect" title="System-on-a-chip">SoC</a> implementation</li>
<li>V – <a href="/wiki/Verilog" title="Verilog">Verilog</a> source file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Value_Change_Dump" class="mw-redirect" title="Value Change Dump">VCD</a> – Standard format for <a href="/wiki/Digital_data" title="Digital data">digital</a> simulation <a href="/wiki/Waveform" title="Waveform">waveform</a></li>
<li>VHD, VHDL – <a href="/wiki/VHDL" title="VHDL">VHDL</a> source file</li>
<li>WGL – Waveform Generation Language, format for Test Patterns for <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">IC</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Test_technology">Test technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&aamp;section=7" title="Edit section: Test technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Files output from <a href="/wiki/Automatic_Test_Equipment" class="mw-redirect" title="Automatic Test Equipment">Automatic Test Equipment</a> or post-processed from such.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Standard_Test_Data_Format" title="Standard Test Data Format">Standard Test Data Format</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Database">Database</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Database">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>4DB – <a href="/wiki/4th_Dimension_(software)" title="4th Dimension (software)">4D</a> database Structure file</li>
<li>4DD – <a href="/wiki/4th_Dimension_(software)" title="4th Dimension (software)">4D</a> database Data file</li>
<li>4DIndy – <a href="/wiki/4th_Dimension_(software)" title="4th Dimension (software)">4D</a> database Structure Index file</li>
<li>4DIndx – <a href="/wiki/4th_Dimension_(software)" title="4th Dimension (software)">4D</a> database Data Index file</li>
<li>4DR – <a href="/wiki/4th_Dimension_(software)" title="4th Dimension (software)">4D</a> database Data resource file (in old 4D versions)</li>
<li>ACCDB – Microsoft Database (<a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Access" title="Microsoft Access">Microsoft Office Access 2007</a> and later)</li>
<li>ACCDE – Compiled Microsoft Database (<a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Access" title="Microsoft Access">Microsoft Office Access 2007</a> and later)</li>
<li>ADT – Sybase <a href="/wiki/Advantage_Database_Server_(ADS)" class="mw-redirect" title="Advantage Database Server (ADS)">Advantage Database Server (ADS)</a></li>
<li>APR – <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Approach" class="mw-redirect" title="Lotus Approach">Lotus Approach</a> data entry &amp; reports</li>
<li>BOX – <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Notes" class="mw-redirect" title="Lotus Notes">Lotus Notes</a> Post Office mail routing database</li>
<li>CHML – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Krasbit_Technologies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Krasbit Technologies (page does not exist)">Krasbit Technologies</a> Encrypted database file for 1 click integration between contact management software and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chameleon_Software&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chameleon Software (page does not exist)">chameleon(tm) line of imaging workflow solutions</a></li>
<li>DAF – Digital Anchor data file</li>
<li>DAT – DOS Basic</li>
<li>DAT – <a href="/wiki/Cach%C3%A9_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Caché (software)">Intersystems Caché</a> database file</li>
<li>DB – <a href="/wiki/Paradox_(database)" title="Paradox (database)">Paradox</a></li>
<li>DB – <a href="/wiki/SQLite" title="SQLite">SQLite</a></li>
<li>DBF – db/dbase II,III,IV and V, Clipper, Harbour/xHarbour, Fox/FoxPro, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_database" class="mw-redirect" title="Oracle database">Oracle</a></li>
<li>DTA – <a href="/wiki/Sage_Sterling" class="mw-redirect" title="Sage Sterling">Sage Sterling</a> database file</li>
<li>EGT – EGT Universal Document, used to compress sql databases to smaller files, may contain original EGT database style.</li>
<li>ESS – EGT SmartSense is a database of files and its compression style. Specific to EGT SmartSense</li>
<li>EAP – <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_Architect_(software)" title="Enterprise Architect (software)">Enterprise Architect</a> Project</li>
<li>FDB – <a href="/wiki/Firebird_(database_server)" title="Firebird (database server)">Firebird</a> Databases</li>
<li>FDB – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Dynamics_NAV" title="Microsoft Dynamics NAV">Navision</a> database file</li>
<li>FP, FP3, FP5, and FP7 – <a href="/wiki/FileMaker_Pro" title="FileMaker Pro">FileMaker Pro</a></li>
<li>FRM – <a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">MySQL</a> table definition</li>
<li>GDB – Borland <a href="/wiki/InterBase" title="InterBase">InterBase</a> Databases</li>
<li>GTABLE – <a href="/wiki/Google_Drive" title="Google Drive">Google Drive</a> <a href="/wiki/Google_Fusion_Tables" title="Google Fusion Tables">Fusion Table</a></li>
<li>KEXI – <a href="/wiki/Kexi" title="Kexi">Kexi</a> database file (<a href="/wiki/SQLite" title="SQLite">SQLite</a>-based)</li>
<li>KEXIC – shortcut to a database connection for a <a href="/wiki/Kexi" title="Kexi">Kexi</a> databases on a server</li>
<li>KEXIS – shortcut to a <a href="/wiki/Kexi" title="Kexi">Kexi</a> database</li>
<li>LDB – Temporary database file, only existing when database is open</li>
<li>MDA – Add-in file for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Access" title="Microsoft Access">Microsoft Access</a></li>
<li>MDB – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Access" title="Microsoft Access">Microsoft Access</a> database</li>
<li>ADP – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Access" title="Microsoft Access">Microsoft Access</a> project (used for accessing databases on a server)</li>
<li>MDE – Compiled Microsoft Database (Access)</li>
<li>MDF – Microsoft SQL Server Database</li>
<li>MYD – MySQL MyISAM table data</li>
<li>MYI – MySQL MyISAM table index</li>
<li>NCF – <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Notes" class="mw-redirect" title="Lotus Notes">Lotus Notes</a> configuration file</li>
<li>NSF – <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Notes" class="mw-redirect" title="Lotus Notes">Lotus Notes</a> database</li>
<li>NTF – <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Notes" class="mw-redirect" title="Lotus Notes">Lotus Notes</a> database design template</li>
<li>NV2 – QW Page <a href="/wiki/NewViews" title="NewViews">NewViews</a> object oriented accounting database</li>
<li>ODB – <a href="/wiki/LibreOffice_Base" title="LibreOffice Base">LibreOffice Base</a> or <a href="/wiki/OpenOffice_Base" class="mw-redirect" title="OpenOffice Base">OpenOffice Base</a> database</li>
<li>ORA – <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle</a> tablespace files sometimes get this extension (also used for configuration files)</li>
<li>PCONTACT – WinIM Contact file</li>
<li>PDB – <a href="/wiki/PDB_(Palm_OS)" title="PDB (Palm OS)">Palm OS Database</a></li>
<li>PDI – <a href="/wiki/Portable_Database_Image" title="Portable Database Image">Portable Database Image</a></li>
<li>PDX – <a href="/wiki/Paradox_(database)" title="Paradox (database)">Corel Paradox</a> database management</li>
<li>PRC – <a href="/wiki/PRC_(Palm_OS)" title="PRC (Palm OS)">Palm OS resource database</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SQL" title="SQL">SQL</a> – bundled SQL queries</li>
<li>REC – <a href="/w/index.php?title=GNU_recutils&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="GNU recutils (page does not exist)">GNU recutils</a> database</li>
<li>REL – Sage <a href="/wiki/Retrieve_4GL" class="mw-redirect" title="Retrieve 4GL">Retrieve 4GL</a> data file</li>
<li>RIN – Sage Retrieve 4GL index file</li>
<li>SDB – <a href="/wiki/StarOffice" title="StarOffice">StarOffice</a>'s StarBase</li>
<li>SDF – SQL Compact Database file</li>
<li>sqlite – <a href="/wiki/SQLite" title="SQLite">SQLite</a></li>
<li>UDL – <a href="/wiki/Universal_Data_Link" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Data Link">Universal Data Link</a></li>
<li>waData – <a href="/wiki/Wakanda_(software)" title="Wakanda (software)">Wakanda (software)</a> database Data file</li>
<li>waIndx – <a href="/wiki/Wakanda_(software)" title="Wakanda (software)">Wakanda (software)</a> database Index file</li>
<li>waModel – <a href="/wiki/Wakanda_(software)" title="Wakanda (software)">Wakanda (software)</a> database Model file</li>
<li>waJournal – <a href="/wiki/Wakanda_(software)" title="Wakanda (software)">Wakanda (software)</a> database Journal file</li>
<li>WDB – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Works" title="Microsoft Works">Microsoft Works</a> Database</li>
<li>WMDB – <a href="/wiki/Windows_Media_Player" title="Windows Media Player">Windows Media</a> Database file – The <code>CurrentDatabase_360.wmdb</code> file can contain file name, file properties, music, video, photo and playlist information.</li></ul>

<ul><li>AI – <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Illustrator" title="Adobe Illustrator">Adobe Illustrator</a></li>

<li>CPT – <a href="/wiki/Corel_Photo-Paint" title="Corel Photo-Paint">Corel Photo-Paint</a></li>

<li>GDRAW – <a href="/wiki/Google_Drive" title="Google Drive">Google Drive</a> Drawing</li>
<li>ILDOC – Broadvision Quicksilver document</li>
<li>INDD – <a href="/wiki/Adobe_InDesign" title="Adobe InDesign">Adobe InDesign</a></li>
<li>MCF – <a href="/wiki/FotoInsight" title="FotoInsight">FotoInsight</a> Designer</li>
<li>PDF – <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Acrobat" title="Adobe Acrobat">Adobe Acrobat</a> or Adobe Reader</li>
<li>PMD – <a href="/wiki/Adobe_PageMaker" title="Adobe PageMaker">Adobe PageMaker</a></li>
<li>PPP – Serif <a href="/wiki/PagePlus" title="PagePlus">PagePlus</a></li>
<li>PSD – <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Photoshop" title="Adobe Photoshop">Adobe Photoshop</a></li>
<li>PUB – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Publisher" title="Microsoft Publisher">Microsoft Publisher</a></li>
<li>QXD – <a href="/wiki/QuarkXPress" title="QuarkXPress">QuarkXPress</a></li>
<li>SLA / SCD – <a href="/wiki/Scribus" title="Scribus">Scribus</a></li>
<li>WFP / WVE — <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wondershare&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wondershare (page does not exist)">Wondershare</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Filmora&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Filmora (page does not exist)">Filmora</a> Project</li>
<li>WLMP – <a href="/wiki/Windows_Live_Movie_Maker" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows Live Movie Maker">Windows Live Movie Maker</a> project</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/XCF_(file_format)" title="XCF (file format)">XCF</a> – File format used by the <a href="/wiki/GIMP" title="GIMP">GIMP</a>, as well as other programs</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Document">Document</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Document">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>These files store <a href="/wiki/Formatted_text" title="Formatted text">formatted text</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plain_text" title="Plain text">plain text</a>.
</p>
<div>

&#32;
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;"><tbody><tr>
<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<ul><li>0   – Plain Text Document, normally used for licensing</li>
<li>1ST – Plain Text Document, normally preceded by the words "README" (README.1ST)</li>
<li>600 – Plain Text Document, used in UNZIP history log</li>
<li>602 – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Text602&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Text602 (page does not exist)">Text602</a> document</li>
<li>ABW – <a href="/wiki/AbiWord" title="AbiWord">AbiWord</a> document</li>

<li>AMI – Lotus Ami Pro</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amigaguide" class="mw-redirect" title="Amigaguide">Amigaguide</a></li>
<li>ANS – <a href="/wiki/American_National_Standards_Institute" title="American National Standards Institute">American National Standards Institute</a> (ANSI) text</li>
<li>ASC – <a href="/wiki/ASCII" title="ASCII">ASCII</a> text</li>
<li>AWW – Ability Write</li>
<li>CCF – Color Chat 1.0</li>

<li>CWK – ClarisWorks-<a href="/wiki/AppleWorks" title="AppleWorks">AppleWorks</a> document</li>
<li>DBK – <a href="/wiki/DocBook" title="DocBook">DocBook</a> XML sub-format</li>
<li>DITA – <a href="/wiki/Darwin_Information_Typing_Architecture" title="Darwin Information Typing Architecture">Darwin Information Typing Architecture</a> document</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DOC_(computing)" class="mw-redirect" title="DOC (computing)">DOC</a> – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Word" title="Microsoft Word">Microsoft Word</a> document</li>

<li>FTX – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fielded_Text&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fielded Text (page does not exist)">Fielded Text</a> (Declared)</li>
<li>GDOC – <a href="/wiki/Google_Drive" title="Google Drive">Google Drive</a> Document</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> – HyperText Markup Language (.html, .htm)</li>
<li>HWP – Haansoft (Hancom) Hangul Word Processor document</li>
<li>HWPML – Haansoft (Hancom) Hangul Word Processor Markup Language document</li>
<li>LOG – Text log file</li>
<li>LWP – <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Word_Pro" class="mw-redirect" title="Lotus Word Pro">Lotus Word Pro</a></li>
<li>MBP – metadata for <a href="/wiki/Mobipocket" title="Mobipocket">Mobipocket</a> documents</li>
<li>MD – <a href="/wiki/Markdown" title="Markdown">Markdown</a> text document</li>
<li>ME – Plain text document normally preceded by the word "READ" (READ.ME)</li>
<li>MCW – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Word" title="Microsoft Word">Microsoft Word</a> for Macintosh (versions 4.0–5.1)</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_records">Financial records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Financial records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>MYO – <a href="/wiki/MYOB_(company)" title="MYOB (company)">MYOB Limited</a> (Windows) File</li>
<li>MYOB – MYOB Limited (Mac) File</li>
<li>TAX – <a href="/wiki/TurboTax" title="TurboTax">TurboTax</a> File</li>
<li>YNAB – <a href="/wiki/You_Need_a_Budget_(YNAB)" class="mw-redirect" title="You Need a Budget (YNAB)">You Need a Budget (YNAB)</a> File</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_data_transfer_formats">Financial data transfer formats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Financial data transfer formats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Interactive Financial Exchange (IFX) – <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a>-based specification for various forms of financial transactions</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Open_Financial_Exchange" title="Open Financial Exchange">Open Financial Exchange</a> (.ofx) – <a href="/wiki/Open_standard" title="Open standard">open standard</a> supported by <a href="/wiki/CheckFree" class="mw-redirect" title="CheckFree">CheckFree</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> and partly by Intuit; <a href="/wiki/SGML" class="mw-redirect" title="SGML">SGML</a> and later <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> based</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/QFX_(file_format)" title="QFX (file format)">QFX</a> – proprietary pay-only format used only by <a href="/wiki/Intuit" title="Intuit">Intuit</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Quicken_Interchange_Format" title="Quicken Interchange Format">Quicken Interchange Format</a> (.qif) – <a href="/wiki/Open_standard" title="Open standard">open standard</a> formerly supported by <a href="/wiki/Intuit" title="Intuit">Intuit</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Font_file">Font file</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Font file">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>ABF – Adobe Binary Screen Font</li>
<li>AFM – Adobe Font Metrics</li>
<li>BDF – <a href="/wiki/Glyph_Bitmap_Distribution_Format" title="Glyph Bitmap Distribution Format">Bitmap Distribution Format</a></li>
<li>BMF – ByteMap Font Format</li>
<li>BRFNT - Binary Revolution Font Format</li>
<li>FNT – <a href="/wiki/Bitmap_font" class="mw-redirect" title="Bitmap font">Bitmapped Font</a> – <a href="/wiki/Graphics_Environment_Manager" class="mw-redirect" title="Graphics Environment Manager">Graphics Environment Manager</a> (GEM)</li>
<li>FON – <a href="/wiki/Bitmap_font" class="mw-redirect" title="Bitmap font">Bitmapped Font</a> – Microsoft Windows</li>
<li>MGF – <a href="/w/index.php?title=MicroGrafx&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="MicroGrafx (page does not exist)">MicroGrafx</a> Font</li>
<li>OTF – <a href="/wiki/OpenType" title="OpenType">OpenType</a> Font</li>
<li>PCF – <a href="/wiki/Portable_Compiled_Format" title="Portable Compiled Format">Portable Compiled Format</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PostScript" title="PostScript">PostScript</a> Font – Type 1, Type 2
<ul><li>PFA – Printer Font ASCII</li>
<li>PFB – Printer Font Binary – Adobe</li>
<li>PFM – Printer Font Metrics – Adobe</li>
<li>AFM – Adobe Font Metrics</li>
<li>FOND – Font Description resource – Mac OS</li></ul></li>
<li>SFD – <a href="/wiki/FontForge" title="FontForge">FontForge</a> spline font database Font</li>
<li>SNF – <a href="/wiki/Server_Normal_Format" title="Server Normal Format">Server Normal Format</a></li>
<li>TDF – TheDraw Font</li>
<li>TFM – <a href="/wiki/TeX_font_metric" title="TeX font metric">TeX font metric</a></li>
<li>TTF (.ttf, .ttc) – <a href="/wiki/TrueType" title="TrueType">TrueType</a> Font</li>
<li>UFO – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Unified_Font_Object&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Unified Font Object (page does not exist)">Unified Font Object</a> is a cross-platform, cross-application, human readable, future proof format for storing font data.</li>
<li>WOFF – <a href="/wiki/Web_Open_Font_Format" title="Web Open Font Format">Web Open Font Format</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_information_system">Geographic information system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Geographic information system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>ASC – ASCII <a href="/wiki/Point_of_interest" title="Point of interest">point of interest</a> (POI) text file</li>
<li>APR – <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Systems_Research_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental Systems Research Institute">ESRI</a> ArcView 3.3 and earlier project file</li>
<li>DEM – <a href="/wiki/USGS_DEM" title="USGS DEM">USGS DEM</a> file format</li>
<li>E00 – ARC/INFO interchange file format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GeoJSON" title="GeoJSON">GeoJSON</a> –Geographically located data in object notation</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GeoTIFF" title="GeoTIFF">GeoTIFF</a> – Geographically located raster data</li>
<li>GML – <a href="/wiki/Geography_Markup_Language" title="Geography Markup Language">Geography Markup Language</a> file<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GPS_eXchange_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="GPS eXchange Format">GPX</a> – XML-based interchange format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Itinerary_file" title="Itinerary file">ITN</a> – <a href="/wiki/TomTom" title="TomTom">TomTom</a> Itinerary format</li>
<li>MXD – ESRI ArcGIS project file, 8.0 and higher</li>
<li>NTF – <a href="/wiki/National_Transfer_Format" title="National Transfer Format">National Transfer Format</a> file</li>
<li>OV2 – <a href="/wiki/TomTom" title="TomTom">TomTom</a> POI overlay file</li>
<li>SHP – ESRI <a href="/wiki/Shapefile" title="Shapefile">shapefile</a></li>
<li>TAB – MapInfo Table file format</li>
<li>World TIFF – Geographically located raster data: text file giving corner coordinate, raster cells per unit, and rotation</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DTED" title="DTED">DTED</a> – Digital Terrain Elevation Data</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/KML" class="mw-redirect" title="KML">KML</a> – <a href="/wiki/Keyhole_Markup_Language" title="Keyhole Markup Language">Keyhole Markup Language</a>, XML-based</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Graphical_information_organizers">Graphical information organizers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Graphical information organizers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=3DT&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="3DT (page does not exist)">3DT</a> – <a href="/wiki/3D_Topicscape" title="3D Topicscape">3D Topicscape</a>, the database in which the meta-data of a 3D Topicscape is held, it is a form of 3D concept map (like a 3D mind-map) used to organize ideas, information, and computer files</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ATY" class="mw-redirect" title="ATY">ATY</a> – <a href="/wiki/3D_Topicscape" title="3D Topicscape">3D Topicscape</a> file, produced when an association type is exported; used to permit round-trip (export Topicscape, change files and folders as desired, re-import to 3D Topicscape)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=CAG_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="CAG (file format) (page does not exist)">CAG</a> – <a href="/wiki/Linear_Reference_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Linear Reference System">Linear Reference System</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=FES_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="FES (file format) (page does not exist)">FES</a> – <a href="/wiki/3D_Topicscape" title="3D Topicscape">3D Topicscape</a> file, produced when a fileless occurrence in 3D Topicscape is exported to Windows. Used to permit round-trip (export Topicscape, change files and folders as desired, re-import them to 3D Topicscape)</li>
<li>MGMF – MindGenius Mind Mapping Software file format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mind_Map" class="mw-redirect" title="Mind Map">MM</a> – <a href="/wiki/FreeMind" title="FreeMind">FreeMind</a> mind map file (XML)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=MMP_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="MMP (file format) (page does not exist)">MMP</a> – <a href="/wiki/Mind_Manager" class="mw-redirect" title="Mind Manager">Mind Manager</a> mind map file</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=TPC_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="TPC (file format) (page does not exist)">TPC</a> – <a href="/wiki/3D_Topicscape" title="3D Topicscape">3D Topicscape</a> file, produced when an inter-Topicscape topic link file is exported to Windows; used to permit round-trip (export Topicscape, change files and folders as desired, re-import to 3D Topicscape)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Graphics">Graphics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Graphics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Image_file_formats" title="Image file formats">image file formats</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Color_palettes">Color palettes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Color palettes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>ACT – Adobe Color Table. Contains a raw color palette and consists of 256 24-bit RGB colour values.</li>
<li>ASE – Adobe Swatch Exchange. Used by Adobe Photoshop, Illustrator, and InDesign.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>GPL – GIMP palette file. Uses a text representation of color names and RGB values. Various open source graphical editors can read this format,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/GIMP" title="GIMP">GIMP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inkscape" title="Inkscape">Inkscape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krita" title="Krita">Krita</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/KolourPaint" title="KolourPaint">KolourPaint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scribus" title="Scribus">Scribus</a>, <a href="/wiki/CinePaint" title="CinePaint">CinePaint</a>, and <a href="/wiki/MyPaint" title="MyPaint">MyPaint</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>PAL – Microsoft <a href="/wiki/Resource_Interchange_File_Format" title="Resource Interchange File Format">RIFF</a> palette file</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Color_management">Color management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Color management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>ICC/ICM – Color profile conforming the specification of the <a href="/wiki/International_Color_Consortium" title="International Color Consortium">ICC</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Raster_graphics">Raster graphics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Raster graphics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Raster_graphics" title="Raster graphics">Raster or bitmap</a> files store images as a group of <a href="/wiki/Pixel" title="Pixel">pixels</a>.
</p>
<div>

&#32;
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;"><tbody><tr>
<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/ART_image_file_format" title="ART image file format">ART</a> – <a href="/wiki/America_Online" class="mw-redirect" title="America Online">America Online</a> proprietary format</li>
<li>BLP – <a href="/wiki/Blizzard_Entertainment" title="Blizzard Entertainment">Blizzard Entertainment</a> proprietary texture format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Windows_bitmap" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows bitmap">BMP</a> – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> Bitmap formatted image</li>
<li>BTI – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> proprietary texture format</li>
<li>CD5 – <a href="/wiki/Chasys_Draw_IES" title="Chasys Draw IES">Chasys Draw IES</a> image</li>
<li>CIT – Intergraph is a monochrome bitmap format</li>
<li>CPT – <a href="/wiki/Corel_PHOTO-PAINT" class="mw-redirect" title="Corel PHOTO-PAINT">Corel PHOTO-PAINT</a> image</li>
<li>CR2 – Canon camera raw format; photos have this on some Canon cameras if the quality <i>RAW</i> is selected in camera settings</li>
<li>CLIP – CLIP STUDIO PAINT format</li>
<li>CPL – Windows control panel file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DirectDraw_Surface" title="DirectDraw Surface">DDS</a> – DirectX texture file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Windows_bitmap" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows bitmap">DIB</a> – Device-Independent Bitmap graphic</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DjVu" title="DjVu">DjVu</a> – DjVu for scanned documents</li>
<li>EGT – EGT Universal Document, used in EGT SmartSense to compress PNG files to yet a smaller file</li>
<li>Exif – <a href="/wiki/Exchangeable_image_file_format" class="mw-redirect" title="Exchangeable image file format">Exchangeable image file format</a> (Exif) is a specification for the image format used by digital cameras</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Graphics_Interchange_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Graphics Interchange Format">GIF</a> – <a href="/wiki/CompuServe" title="CompuServe">CompuServe</a>'s Graphics Interchange Format</li>
<li>GRF – <a href="/wiki/Zebra_Technologies" title="Zebra Technologies">Zebra Technologies</a> proprietary format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Apple_Icon_Image" class="mw-redirect" title="Apple Icon Image">ICNS</a> – format for <i><a href="/wiki/Icon_(computing)" title="Icon (computing)">icons</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a>. Contains bitmap images at multiple resolutions and bitdepths with <a href="/wiki/Alpha_channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Alpha channel">alpha channel</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ICO_(icon_image_file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="ICO (icon image file format)">ICO</a> – a format used for <i><a href="/wiki/Icon_(computing)" title="Icon (computing)">icons</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>. Contains small bitmap images at multiple resolutions and bitdepths with 1-bit transparency or alpha channel.</li>
<li>IFF (.iff, .ilbm, .lbm) – <a href="/wiki/ILBM" title="ILBM">ILBM</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JPEG_Network_Graphics" title="JPEG Network Graphics">JNG</a> – a single-frame <a href="/wiki/Multiple-image_Network_Graphics" title="Multiple-image Network Graphics">MNG</a> using <a href="/wiki/JPEG" title="JPEG">JPEG</a> compression and possibly an <a href="/wiki/Alpha_channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Alpha channel">alpha channel</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JPEG" title="JPEG">JPEG</a>, JFIF (.jpg or .jpeg) – Joint Photographic Experts Group; a lossy image format widely used to display photographic images</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JPEG_2000" title="JPEG 2000">JP2</a> – JPEG2000</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JPEG_Stereo" class="mw-redirect" title="JPEG Stereo">JPS</a> – JPEG Stereo</li>
<li>LBM – <a href="/wiki/Deluxe_Paint" title="Deluxe Paint">Deluxe Paint</a> image file</li>
<li>MAX – ScanSoft <a href="/wiki/PaperPort" title="PaperPort">PaperPort</a> document</li>
<li>MIFF – <a href="/wiki/ImageMagick" title="ImageMagick">ImageMagick</a>'s native file format</li>
<li>MNG – <a href="/wiki/Multiple-image_Network_Graphics" title="Multiple-image Network Graphics">Multiple-image Network Graphics</a>, the animated version of <a href="/wiki/Portable_Network_Graphics" title="Portable Network Graphics">PNG</a></li>
<li>MSP – a format used by old versions of Microsoft Paint; replaced by <a href="/wiki/BMP_file_format" title="BMP file format">BMP</a> in <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> 3.0</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NITF_(National_Imagery_Transmission_Format)" class="mw-redirect" title="NITF (National Imagery Transmission Format)">NITF</a> – A U.S. Government standard commonly used in <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_(information_gathering)" class="mw-redirect" title="Intelligence (information gathering)">Intelligence</a> systems</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OTA_bitmap" title="OTA bitmap">OTB</a> – Over The Air bitmap, a specification designed by <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a> for black and white images for <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile phones</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Portable_bitmap" class="mw-redirect" title="Portable bitmap">PBM</a> – Portable bitmap</li>
<li>PC1 – Low resolution, compressed Degas picture file</li>
<li>PC2 – Medium resolution, compressed Degas picture file</li>
<li>PC3 – High resolution, compressed Degas picture file</li>
<li>PCF – Pixel Coordination Format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PCX" title="PCX">PCX</a> – a lossless format used by ZSoft's PC Paint, popular for a time on <a href="/wiki/DOS" title="DOS">DOS</a> systems.</li>
<li>PDN – <a href="/wiki/Paint.NET" class="mw-redirect" title="Paint.NET">Paint.NET</a> image file</li>
<li>PGM – <a href="/wiki/Portable_graymap" class="mw-redirect" title="Portable graymap">Portable graymap</a></li>
<li>PI1 – Low resolution, uncompressed Degas picture file</li>
<li>PI2 – Medium resolution, uncompressed Degas picture file; also Portrait Innovations encrypted image format</li>
<li>PI3 – High resolution, uncompressed Degas picture file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PICT" title="PICT">PICT</a>, PCT – Apple <a href="/wiki/Macintosh" title="Macintosh">Macintosh</a> PICT image</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Portable_Network_Graphics" title="Portable Network Graphics">PNG</a> – Portable Network Graphic (lossless, recommended for display and edition of graphic images)</li>
<li>PNM – <a href="/wiki/Portable_anymap" class="mw-redirect" title="Portable anymap">Portable anymap</a> graphic bitmap image</li>
<li>PNS – PNG Stereo</li>
<li>PPM – <a href="/wiki/Portable_Pixmap" class="mw-redirect" title="Portable Pixmap">Portable Pixmap</a> (Pixel Map) image</li>
<li>PSB – Adobe Photoshop Big image file (for large files)</li>
<li>PSD, PDD – <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Photoshop" title="Adobe Photoshop">Adobe Photoshop</a> Drawing</li>
<li>PSP – <a href="/wiki/Paint_Shop_Pro" class="mw-redirect" title="Paint Shop Pro">Paint Shop Pro</a> image</li>
<li>PX – Pixel image editor image file</li>
<li>PXM – <a href="/wiki/Pixelmator" title="Pixelmator">Pixelmator</a> image file</li>
<li>PXR – <a href="/wiki/Pixar_Image_Computer" title="Pixar Image Computer">Pixar Image Computer</a> image file</li>
<li>QFX – QuickLink Fax image</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Raw_image_format" title="Raw image format">RAW</a> – General term for minimally processed image data (acquired by a <a href="/wiki/Digital_camera" title="Digital camera">digital camera</a>)</li>
<li>RLE – a <a href="/wiki/Run-length_encoding" title="Run-length encoding">run-length encoding</a> image</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scitex_CT_(Continuous_Tone)_Bitmap_Image_File_%E2%80%93_.sct&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Scitex CT (Continuous Tone) Bitmap Image File – .sct (page does not exist)">SCT</a> – Scitex Continuous Tone image file</li>
<li>SGI, RGB, INT, BW – <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Graphics_Image" title="Silicon Graphics Image">Silicon Graphics Image</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Truevision_Targa_File_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Truevision Targa File Format">TGA</a> (.tga, .targa, .icb, .vda, .vst, .pix) – <a href="/wiki/Truevision" title="Truevision">Truevision</a> TGA (Targa) image</li>
<li>TIFF (.tif or .tiff) – <a href="/wiki/Tagged_Image_File_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Tagged Image File Format">Tagged Image File Format</a> (usually lossless, but many variants exist, including lossy ones)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TIFF/EP" title="TIFF/EP">TIFF/EP</a> (.tif or .tiff) – Tag Image File Format / Electronic Photography, ISO 12234-2; tends to be used as a basis for other formats rather than in its own right.</li>
<li>VTF – Valve Texture Format</li>
<li>XBM – <a href="/wiki/X_Window_System" title="X Window System">X Window System</a> Bitmap</li>
<li>XCF – <a href="/wiki/GIMP" title="GIMP">GIMP</a> image (from Gimp's origin at the <a href="/wiki/EXperimental_Computing_Facility" title="EXperimental Computing Facility">eXperimental Computing Facility</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/XPM_(image_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="XPM (image format)">XPM</a> – X Window System Pixmap</li>
<li>ZIF – Zoomable/Zoomify Image Format (a web-friendly, TIFF-based, zoomable image format)</li></ul>
<p>&#32;
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vector_graphics">Vector graphics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Vector graphics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Vector_graphics" title="Vector graphics">Vector graphics</a> use geometric primitives such as points, lines, curves, and polygons to represent images.
</p>
