<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=3DV_file&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="3DV file (page does not exist)">3DV</a> – 3-D wireframe graphics by Oscar Garcia</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Additive_Manufacturing_File_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Additive Manufacturing File Format">AMF</a> – Additive Manufacturing File Format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ability_Draw" class="mw-redirect" title="Ability Draw">AWG</a> – Ability Draw</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adobe_Illustrator_Artwork" title="Adobe Illustrator Artwork">AI</a> – <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Illustrator" title="Adobe Illustrator">Adobe Illustrator</a> Document</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Computer_Graphics_Metafile" title="Computer Graphics Metafile">CGM</a> – Computer Graphics Metafile, an <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardization" title="International Organization for Standardization">ISO</a> Standard</li>
<li>CDR – <a href="/wiki/CorelDRAW" title="CorelDRAW">CorelDRAW</a> Document</li>
<li>CMX – <a href="/wiki/CorelDRAW" title="CorelDRAW">CorelDRAW</a> vector image</li>
<li>DP – Drawing Program file for <a href="/wiki/PERQ" title="PERQ">PERQ</a> <sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AutoCAD_DXF" title="AutoCAD DXF">DXF</a> – ASCII Drawing Interchange file Format, used in <a href="/wiki/AutoCAD" title="AutoCAD">AutoCAD</a> and other CAD-programs</li>
<li>E2D – 2-dimensional vector graphics used by the editor which is included in <a href="/wiki/JFire" title="JFire">JFire</a></li>
<li>EGT – EGT Universal Document, EGT Vector Draw images are used to draw vector to a website</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Encapsulated_PostScript" title="Encapsulated PostScript">EPS</a> – Encapsulated Postscript</li>
<li>FS – FlexiPro file</li>
<li>GBR – <a href="/wiki/Gerber_file" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerber file">Gerber file</a></li>
<li>ODG – <a href="/wiki/OpenDocument" title="OpenDocument">OpenDocument</a> Drawing
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=MOVIE.BYU&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="MOVIE.BYU (page does not exist)">MOVIE.BYU</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/RenderMan_Interface_Specification" title="RenderMan Interface Specification">RenderMan</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scalable_Vector_Graphics" title="Scalable Vector Graphics">SVG</a> – Scalable Vector Graphics, employs <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scene_description_language" title="Scene description language">Scene description languages</a> (3D vector image formats)
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/STL_(file_format)" title="STL (file format)">STL</a> – Stereo Lithographic data format (see <a href="/wiki/STL_(file_format)" title="STL (file format)">STL (file format)</a>) used by various CAD systems and stereo lithographic printing machines. See above.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/VRML" title="VRML">VRML</a> Uses .wrl extension – Virtual Reality Modeling Language, for the creation of 3D viewable web images.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/X3D" title="X3D">X3D</a></li></ul></li>
<li>SXD – <a href="/wiki/OpenOffice.org_XML" title="OpenOffice.org XML">OpenOffice.org XML</a> (obsolete) Drawing</li>
<li>V2D – voucher design used by the voucher management included in <a href="/wiki/JFire" title="JFire">JFire</a></li>
<li>VDOC – Vector format used in AnyCut, CutStorm, DrawCut, DragonCut, FutureDRAW, MasterCut, SignMaster, VinylMaster software by Future Corporation</li>
<li>VSD – Vector format used by <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Visio" title="Microsoft Visio">Microsoft Visio</a></li>
<li>VSDX – Vector format used by MS Visio and opened by <a href="/wiki/Vsdx_annotator" class="mw-redirect" title="Vsdx annotator">VSDX Annotator</a></li>
<li>VND – Vision numeric Drawing file used in TypeEdit, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gravostyle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gravostyle (page does not exist)">Gravostyle</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Windows_Metafile" title="Windows Metafile">WMF</a> – Windows Meta File</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/EMF_File_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="EMF File Format">EMF</a> – Enhanced (Windows) MetaFile, an extension to WMF</li>
<li>ART – <a href="/wiki/Xara" title="Xara">Xara</a> – Drawing (superseded by XAR)</li>
<li>XAR – <a href="/wiki/Xara" title="Xara">Xara</a> – Drawing</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="3D_graphics">3D graphics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 3D graphics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://edutechwiki.unige.ch/en/3D_file_format">3D file format</a> at EduTech Wiki</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/3D_computer_graphics" title="3D computer graphics">3D graphics</a> are 3D models that allow building models in real-time or non-real-time 3D rendering.
</p>
<ul><li>3DMF – <a href="/wiki/3DMF" class="mw-redirect" title="3DMF">QuickDraw 3D Metafile</a> (.3dmf)</li>
<li>3DM – <a href="/wiki/OpenNURBS_Initiative" class="mw-redirect" title="OpenNURBS Initiative">OpenNURBS Initiative</a> 3D Model (used by Rhinoceros 3D) (.3dm)</li>
<li>3MF – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> 3D Manufacturing Format (.3mf)<sup id="cite_ref-msdn.microsoft.com_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msdn.microsoft.com-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/.3ds" title=".3ds">3DS</a> – <a href="/wiki/Autodesk_3ds_Max#History" title="Autodesk 3ds Max">legacy 3D Studio</a> Model (.3ds)</li>
<li>ABC – <a href="/wiki/Alembic_(computer_graphics)" title="Alembic (computer graphics)">Alembic (computer graphics)</a></li>
<li>AC – <a href="/wiki/AC3D" title="AC3D">AC3D</a> Model (.ac)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Additive_Manufacturing_File_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Additive Manufacturing File Format">AMF</a> – Additive Manufacturing File Format</li>
<li>AN8 – <a href="/wiki/Anim8or" title="Anim8or">Anim8or</a> Model (.an8)</li>
<li>AOI – Art of Illusion Model (.aoi)</li>
<li>ASM – <a href="/wiki/PTC_Creo" title="PTC Creo">PTC Creo</a> assembly (.asm)</li>
<li>B3D – <a href="/wiki/Blitz_Basic" class="mw-redirect" title="Blitz Basic">Blitz3D</a> Model (.b3d)</li>
<li>BLEND – <a href="/wiki/Blender_(software)" title="Blender (software)">Blender</a> (.blend)</li>
<li>BLOCK – <a href="/wiki/Blender_(software)" title="Blender (software)">Blender</a> encrypted blend files (.block)</li>
<li>BMD3 – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> <a href="/wiki/GameCube" title="GameCube">GameCube</a> first-party J3D proprietary model format (.bmd)</li>
<li>BDL4 – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> <a href="/wiki/GameCube" title="GameCube">GameCube</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> first-party J3D proprietary model format (2002, 2006–2010) (.bdl)</li>
<li>BRRES – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> first-party proprietary model format 2010+ (.brres)</li>
<li>BFRES – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> <a href="/wiki/Wii_U" title="Wii U">Wii U</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Switch" title="Nintendo Switch">Switch</a> first-party proprietary model format</li>
<li>C4D – <a href="/wiki/Cinema_4D" title="Cinema 4D">Cinema 4D</a> (.c4d)</li>
<li>Cal3D – <a href="/wiki/Cal3D" title="Cal3D">Cal3D</a> (.cal3d)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CCP4_(file_format)" title="CCP4 (file format)">CCP4</a> – X-ray crystallography voxels (electron density)</li>
<li>CFL – <a href="/wiki/Compressed_File_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="Compressed File Library">Compressed File Library</a> (.cfl)</li>
<li>COB – <a href="/wiki/TrueSpace" title="TrueSpace">Caligari Object</a> (.cob)</li>
<li>CORE3D – Coreona 3D Coreona 3D Virtual File(.core3d)</li>
<li>CTM – <a href="/wiki/OpenCTM" title="OpenCTM">OpenCTM</a> (.ctm)</li>
<li>DAE – <a href="/wiki/COLLADA" title="COLLADA">COLLADA</a> (.dae)</li>
<li>DFF – <a href="/wiki/RenderWare" title="RenderWare">RenderWare</a> binary stream, commonly used by <a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_III" title="Grand Theft Auto III">Grand Theft Auto III</a>-era games as well as other RenderWare titles</li>
<li>DPM – <a href="/w/index.php?title=DeepMesh&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="DeepMesh (page does not exist)">deepMesh</a> (.dpm)</li>
<li>DTS – <a href="/wiki/Torque_Game_Engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Torque Game Engine">Torque Game Engine</a> (<a href="/w/index.php?title=DTS_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="DTS (file format) (page does not exist)">.dts</a>)</li>
<li>EGG – <a href="/wiki/Panda3D" title="Panda3D">Panda3D</a> Engine</li>
<li>FACT – <a href="/wiki/Electric_Image" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric Image">Electric Image</a> (.fac)</li>
<li>FBX – Autodesk <a href="/wiki/FBX" title="FBX">FBX</a> (.fbx)</li>
<li>G – <a href="/wiki/BRL-CAD" title="BRL-CAD">BRL-CAD</a> geometry (.g)</li>
<li>GLB – a binary form of <a href="/wiki/GlTF" title="GlTF">glTF</a> required to be loaded in <a href="/wiki/Facebook_3D_Posts" title="Facebook 3D Posts">Facebook 3D Posts</a>. (.glb)</li>
<li>GLM – Ghoul Mesh (.glm)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GlTF" title="GlTF">glTF</a> – the JSON standard developed by <a href="/wiki/Khronos_Group" title="Khronos Group">Khronos Group</a> (.gltf)</li>
<li>IOB – <a href="/wiki/Imagine_(3D_modeling_software)" title="Imagine (3D modeling software)">Imagine (3D modeling software)</a> (.iob)</li>
<li>JAS – <a href="/wiki/Cheetah_3D" class="mw-redirect" title="Cheetah 3D">Cheetah 3D</a> file (.jas)</li>
<li>LWO – <a href="/wiki/Lightwave" class="mw-redirect" title="Lightwave">Lightwave</a> Object (.lwo)</li>
<li>LWS – <a href="/wiki/Lightwave" class="mw-redirect" title="Lightwave">Lightwave</a> Scene (.lws)</li>
<li>LXF – <a href="/wiki/LEGO_Digital_Designer" class="mw-redirect" title="LEGO Digital Designer">LEGO Digital Designer</a> Model file (.lxf)</li>
<li>LXO – Luxology <a href="/wiki/Modo_(software)" title="Modo (software)">Modo (software)</a> file (.lxo)</li>
<li>MA – Autodesk <a href="/wiki/Maya_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maya (software)">Maya</a> ASCII File (.ma)</li>
<li>MAX – Autodesk <a href="/wiki/3D_Studio_Max" class="mw-redirect" title="3D Studio Max">3D Studio Max</a> file (.max)</li>
<li>MB – Autodesk <a href="/wiki/Maya_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maya (software)">Maya</a> Binary File (.mb)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MD2_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="MD2 (file format)">MD2</a> – <a href="/wiki/Quake_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Quake 2">Quake 2</a> model format (.md2)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MD3_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="MD3 (file format)">MD3</a> – <a href="/wiki/Quake_3" class="mw-redirect" title="Quake 3">Quake 3</a> model format (.md3)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MD5_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="MD5 (file format)">MD5</a> – <a href="/wiki/Doom_3" title="Doom 3">Doom 3</a> model format (.md5)</li>
<li>MDX – <a href="/wiki/Blizzard_Entertainment" title="Blizzard Entertainment">Blizzard Entertainment</a>'s own model format (.mdx)</li>
<li>MESH – New York University(.m)</li>
<li>MESH – Meshwork Model (.mesh)</li>
<li>MM3D – Misfit Model 3d (.mm3d)</li>
<li>MPO – Multi-Picture Object – This <a href="/wiki/.mpo#JPEG_Multi-Picture_Format" class="mw-redirect" title=".mpo">JPEG</a> standard is used for 3d images, as with the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_3DS" title="Nintendo 3DS">Nintendo 3DS</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MRC_(file_format)" title="MRC (file format)">MRC</a> – voxels in cryo-electron microscopy</li>
<li>NIF – <a href="/wiki/Gamebryo" title="Gamebryo">Gamebryo</a> NetImmerse File (.nif)</li>
<li>OBJ – <a href="/wiki/Wavefront_.obj_file" title="Wavefront .obj file">Wavefront .obj file</a> (.obj)</li>
<li>OFF – <a href="/wiki/OFF_(file_format)" title="OFF (file format)">OFF Object file format</a> (.off)</li>
<li>OGEX – <a href="/wiki/Open_Game_Engine_Exchange" title="Open Game Engine Exchange">Open Game Engine Exchange</a> (OpenGEX) format (.ogex)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PLY_(file_format)" title="PLY (file format)">PLY</a> – Polygon File Format / Stanford Triangle Format (.ply)</li>
<li>PRC – Adobe <a href="/wiki/PRC_(file_format)" title="PRC (file format)">PRC</a> (embedded in <a href="/wiki/PDF" title="PDF">PDF</a> files)</li>
<li>PRT – <a href="/wiki/PTC_Creo" title="PTC Creo">PTC Creo</a> part (.prt)</li>
<li>POV – <a href="/wiki/POV-Ray" title="POV-Ray">POV-Ray</a> document (.pov)</li>
<li>R3D – <a href="/wiki/Realsoft_3D" title="Realsoft 3D">Realsoft 3D</a> (Real-3D) (.r3d)</li>
<li>RWX – <a href="/wiki/RenderWare" title="RenderWare">RenderWare</a> Object (.rwx)</li>
<li>SIA – Nevercenter Silo Object (.sia)</li>
<li>SIB – Nevercenter Silo Object (.sib)</li>
<li>SKP – <a href="/wiki/Google_Sketchup" class="mw-redirect" title="Google Sketchup">Google Sketchup</a> file (.skp)</li>
<li>SLDASM – <a href="/wiki/SolidWorks" title="SolidWorks">SolidWorks</a> Assembly Document (.sldasm)</li>
<li>SLDPRT – <a href="/wiki/SolidWorks" title="SolidWorks">SolidWorks</a> Part Document (.sldprt)</li>
<li>SMD – <a href="/wiki/Valve_Corporation" title="Valve Corporation">Valve</a> Studiomdl Data format (.smd)</li>
<li>U3D – <a href="/wiki/Universal_3D" title="Universal 3D">Universal 3D</a> format (.u3d)</li>
<li>USD – <a href="/wiki/Showplace#Universal_scene_description" title="Showplace">Universal Scene Description</a> (.usd)</li>
<li>USDA – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://graphics.pixar.com/usd/docs/Converting-Between-Layer-Formats.html">Universal Scene Description , Human-readable text format</a> (.usda)</li>
<li>USDC – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://graphics.pixar.com/usd/docs/Converting-Between-Layer-Formats.html">Universal Scene Description , Binary format</a> (.usdc)</li>
<li>USDZ – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://graphics.pixar.com/usd/docs/Usdz-File-Format-Specification.html">Universal Scene Description Zip</a>  (.usdz)</li>
<li>VIM – <a href="/wiki/Revizto" title="Revizto">Revizto</a> visual information model format (.vimproj)</li>
<li>VRML97 – <a href="/wiki/VRML" title="VRML">VRML</a> Virtual reality modeling language (.wrl)</li>
<li>VUE – <a href="/wiki/E-on_Vue" title="E-on Vue">Vue</a> scene file (.vue)</li>
<li>VWX – Vectorworks (.vwx)</li>
<li>WINGS – <a href="/wiki/Wings3D" class="mw-redirect" title="Wings3D">Wings3D</a> (.wings)</li>
<li>W3D – Westwood 3D Model (.w3d)</li>
<li>X – <a href="/wiki/DirectX" title="DirectX">DirectX 3D Model</a> (.x)</li>
<li>X3D – <a href="/wiki/Extensible_3D" class="mw-redirect" title="Extensible 3D">Extensible 3D</a> (.x3d)</li>
<li>Z3D – <a href="/wiki/Zmodeler" title="Zmodeler">Zmodeler</a> (.z3d)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Links_and_shortcuts">Links and shortcuts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Links and shortcuts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Alias_(Mac_OS)" title="Alias (Mac OS)">Alias (Mac OS)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JNLP" class="mw-redirect" title="JNLP">JNLP</a> – Java Network Launching Protocol, an <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> file used by <a href="/wiki/Java_Web_Start" title="Java Web Start">Java Web Start</a> for starting Java applets over the Internet</li>
<li>LNK – binary-format <a href="/wiki/File_shortcut" class="mw-redirect" title="File shortcut">file shortcut</a> in <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> 95 and later</li>
<li>APPREF-MS – <a href="/wiki/File_shortcut" class="mw-redirect" title="File shortcut">File shortcut</a> format used by <a href="/wiki/ClickOnce" title="ClickOnce">ClickOnce</a></li>
<li>URL – <a href="/wiki/INI_file" title="INI file">INI file</a> pointing to a <a href="/wiki/URL" title="URL">URL</a> <a href="/wiki/Bookmark_(World_Wide_Web)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bookmark (World Wide Web)">bookmarks</a>/Internet shortcut in <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a></li>
<li>WEBLOC – <a href="/wiki/Property_list" title="Property list">Property list</a> file pointing to a <a href="/wiki/URL" title="URL">URL</a> <a href="/wiki/Bookmark_(World_Wide_Web)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bookmark (World Wide Web)">bookmarks</a>/Internet shortcut in <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a></li>
<li>SYM – Symbolic link</li>
<li>.desktop – Desktop entry on <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> <a href="/wiki/Desktop_environments" class="mw-redirect" title="Desktop environments">Desktop environments</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mathematical">Mathematical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Mathematical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Harwell-Boeing_file_format" title="Harwell-Boeing file format">Harwell-Boeing file format</a> – a format designed to store <a href="/wiki/Sparse_matrix" title="Sparse matrix">sparse matrices</a></li>
<li>MML – <a href="/wiki/MathML" title="MathML">MathML</a> – Mathematical Markup Language</li>
<li>ODF – <a href="/wiki/OpenDocument" title="OpenDocument">OpenDocument</a> Math Formula</li>
<li>SXM – <a href="/wiki/OpenOffice.org_XML" title="OpenOffice.org XML">OpenOffice.org XML</a> (obsolete) Math Formula</li></ul>
<h2><span id="Object_code.2C_executable_files.2C_shared_and_dynamically_linked_libraries"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Object_code,_executable_files,_shared_and_dynamically_linked_libraries">Object code, executable files, shared and dynamically linked libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Object code, executable files, shared and dynamically linked libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/8BF" class="mw-redirect" title="8BF">.8BF files</a> – plugins for some photo editing programs including <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Photoshop" title="Adobe Photoshop">Adobe Photoshop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paint_Shop_Pro" class="mw-redirect" title="Paint Shop Pro">Paint Shop Pro</a>, <a href="/wiki/GIMP" title="GIMP">GIMP</a> and <a href="/wiki/Helicon_Filter" title="Helicon Filter">Helicon Filter</a>.</li>
<li>.a – Objective C native static library</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/A.out_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="A.out (file format)">a.out</a> – (no suffix for executable image, .o for object files, .so for <a href="/wiki/Shared_object" class="mw-redirect" title="Shared object">shared object</a> files) classic <a href="/wiki/UNIX" class="mw-redirect" title="UNIX">UNIX</a> object format, now often superseded by ELF</li>
<li>APK – <a href="/wiki/Android_application_package" title="Android application package">Android Application Package</a></li>
<li>APP – A folder found on macOS systems containing program code and resources, appearing as one file.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=BAC_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="BAC (file format) (page does not exist)">BAC</a> – an executable image for the <a href="/wiki/RSTS/E" title="RSTS/E">RSTS/E</a> system, created using the <a href="/wiki/BASIC-PLUS" title="BASIC-PLUS">BASIC-PLUS</a> <tt>COMPILE</tt> command<sup id="cite_ref-dec-11-orsua-d-d_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dec-11-orsua-d-d-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=BPL_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="BPL (file format) (page does not exist)">BPL</a> – a Win32 PE file created with <a href="/wiki/Borland_Delphi" class="mw-redirect" title="Borland Delphi">Borland Delphi</a> or <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2BBuilder" title="C++Builder">C++Builder</a> containing a package.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bundle_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bundle (file format) (page does not exist)">Bundle</a> – a Macintosh plugin created with <a href="/wiki/Xcode" title="Xcode">Xcode</a> or <a href="/wiki/Make_(software)" title="Make (software)">make</a> which holds executable code, data files, and folders for that code.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Class_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="Class (file format)">.Class</a> – used in <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/COFF" title="COFF">COFF</a> (no suffix for executable image, .o for object files) – UNIX Common Object File Format, now often superseded by ELF</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/COM_file" title="COM file">COM files</a> – commands used in <a href="/wiki/DOS" title="DOS">DOS</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Delphi_programming_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Delphi programming language">DCU</a> – <a href="/wiki/Borland_Delphi" class="mw-redirect" title="Borland Delphi">Delphi</a> compiled unit</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dynamic-link_library" title="Dynamic-link library">DLL</a> – library used in Windows and OS/2 to store data, resources and code.</li>
<li>DOL – the format used by the <a href="/wiki/GameCube" title="GameCube">GameCube</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a>, short for Dolphin, which was the codename of the GameCube.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/EAR_(file_format)" title="EAR (file format)">.EAR</a> – archives of Java <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_application" class="mw-redirect" title="Enterprise application">enterprise applications</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Executable_and_Linkable_Format" title="Executable and Linkable Format">ELF</a> – (no suffix for executable image, .o for object files, .so for shared object files) used in many modern <a href="/wiki/Unix" title="Unix">Unix</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unix-like" title="Unix-like">Unix-like</a> systems, including <a href="/wiki/Solaris_(operating_system)" title="Solaris (operating system)">Solaris</a>, other <a href="/wiki/UNIX_System_V" title="UNIX System V">System V Release 4</a> derivatives, <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>, and <a href="/wiki/BSD" class="mw-redirect" title="BSD">BSD</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Expander_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Expander (file format) (page does not exist)">expander</a> (see bundle)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DOS_executable" class="mw-redirect" title="DOS executable">DOS executable</a> (<a href="/wiki/EXE" class="mw-redirect" title="EXE">.exe</a> – used in <a href="/wiki/DOS" title="DOS">DOS</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/.ipa_(file_extension)" class="mw-redirect" title=".ipa (file extension)">.IPA</a> – apple IOS application executable file. Another form of zip file.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=JEFF&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="JEFF (page does not exist)">JEFF</a> – a file format allowing execution directly from static memory<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JAR_(file_format)" title="JAR (file format)">.JAR</a> – archives of Java class files</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/XPInstall" title="XPInstall">.XPI</a> – <a href="/wiki/PKZIP" title="PKZIP">PKZIP</a> archive that can be run by <a href="/wiki/Mozilla" title="Mozilla">Mozilla</a> <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browsers</a> to install software.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mach-O" title="Mach-O">Mach-O</a> – (no suffix for executable image, .o for object files, .dylib and .bundle for shared object files) <a href="/wiki/Mach_kernel" class="mw-redirect" title="Mach kernel">Mach</a>-based systems, notably native format of <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>, <a href="/wiki/WatchOS" title="WatchOS">watchOS</a>, and <a href="/wiki/TvOS" title="TvOS">tvOS</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NetWare_Loadable_Module" title="NetWare Loadable Module">NetWare Loadable Module</a> (.NLM) – the native 32-bit binaries compiled for Novell's <a href="/wiki/NetWare" title="NetWare">NetWare</a> Operating System (versions 3 and newer)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_Executable" title="New Executable">New Executable</a> (.<a href="/wiki/EXE" class="mw-redirect" title="EXE">EXE</a> – used in multitasking ("European") MS-DOS 4.0, <a href="/wiki/16-bit" class="mw-redirect" title="16-bit">16-bit</a> <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>, and <a href="/wiki/OS/2" title="OS/2">OS/2</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/XCOFF" title="XCOFF">.o</a> – un-linked object files directly from the compiler</li>
<li>Obb – a <b>file</b> that developers create along with some APK packages to support the application.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Portable_Executable" title="Portable Executable">Portable Executable</a> (.<a href="/wiki/EXE" class="mw-redirect" title="EXE">EXE</a>,  – used in <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and some other systems)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Preferred_Executable_Format" title="Preferred Executable Format">Preferred Executable Format</a> – (<a href="/wiki/Classic_Mac_OS" title="Classic Mac OS">classic Mac OS</a> for <a href="/wiki/PowerPC" title="PowerPC">PowerPC</a> applications; compatible with <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a> via a classic (Mac OS X) emulator)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=RLL_file_format&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="RLL file format (page does not exist)">RLL</a> – used in Microsoft operating systems together with a DLL file to store program resources</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=S1ES&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="S1ES (page does not exist)">.s1es</a> – <a href="/wiki/Executable" title="Executable">Executable</a> used for S1ES learning system.</li>
<li>.so – shared library, typically ELF</li>
<li>Value Added Process (.VAP) – the native 16-bit binaries compiled for Novell's <a href="/wiki/NetWare" title="NetWare">NetWare</a> Operating System (version 2, NetWare 286, Advanced NetWare, etc.)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WAR_(Sun_file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="WAR (Sun file format)">.WAR</a> – archives of Java <a href="/wiki/Web_application" title="Web application">Web applications</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xbox_executable" class="mw-redirect" title="Xbox executable">XBE</a> – Xbox executable</li>
<li>.XAP – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Windows_Phone_package&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Windows Phone package (page does not exist)">Windows Phone package</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/XCOFF" title="XCOFF">XCOFF</a> – (no suffix for executable image, .o for object files, .a for shared object files) extended COFF, used in <a href="/wiki/AIX_(operating_system)" class="mw-redirect" title="AIX (operating system)">AIX</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">XEX</a> – Xbox 360 executable</li>
<li>Object extensions
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Visual_Basic_Extension" title="Visual Basic Extension">.VBX</a> – Visual Basic extensions</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Component_Object_Model" title="Component Object Model">.OCX</a> – Object Control extensions</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Component_Object_Model" title="Component Object Model">.TLB</a> – Windows Type Library</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Page_description_language">Page description language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Page description language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/DVI_file_format" class="mw-redirect" title="DVI file format">DVI</a> – Device independent format</li>
<li>EGT – Universal Document can be used to store CSS type styles (*.egt)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=PhotoLine_Document&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="PhotoLine Document (page does not exist)">PLD</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Printer_Control_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Printer Control Language">PCL</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Portable_Document_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Portable Document Format">PDF</a> – Portable Document Format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PostScript" title="PostScript">PostScript</a> (.ps, .ps.gz)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SNP_file_format" title="SNP file format">SNP</a> – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Access" title="Microsoft Access">Microsoft Access</a> Report Snapshot</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/XML_Paper_Specification" class="mw-redirect" title="XML Paper Specification">XPS</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/XSL_Formatting_Objects" title="XSL Formatting Objects">XSL-FO (Formatting Objects)</a></li>
<li>Configurations, Metadata
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" title="Cascading Style Sheets">CSS</a> – Cascading Style Sheets</li>
<li>XSLT, XSL – <a href="/wiki/XSL_Transformations" class="mw-redirect" title="XSL Transformations">XML Style Sheet</a> (.xslt, .xsl)</li>
<li>TPL – <a href="/wiki/Web_template" class="mw-redirect" title="Web template">Web template</a> (.tpl)</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_information_manager">Personal information manager</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Personal information manager">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Personal_information_manager" title="Personal information manager">Personal information manager</a></div>
<ul><li>MSG – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Outlook" title="Microsoft Outlook">Microsoft Outlook</a> task manager</li>
<li>ORG – <a href="/wiki/IBM_Lotus_Organizer" title="IBM Lotus Organizer">Lotus Organizer</a> PIM package</li>
<li>PST, OST – Microsoft Outlook email communication</li>
<li>SC2 – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Schedule_Plus" title="Microsoft Schedule Plus">Microsoft Schedule+</a> calendar</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presentation">Presentation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Presentation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>GSLIDES – <a href="/wiki/Google_Drive" title="Google Drive">Google Drive</a> Presentation</li>
<li>KEY, KEYNOTE – <a href="/wiki/Apple_Keynote" class="mw-redirect" title="Apple Keynote">Apple Keynote</a> Presentation</li>
<li>NB – <a href="/wiki/Mathematica" class="mw-redirect" title="Mathematica">Mathematica</a> Slideshow</li>
<li>NBP – Mathematica Player slideshow</li>
<li>ODP – <a href="/wiki/OpenDocument" title="OpenDocument">OpenDocument</a> Presentation</li>
<li>OTP – OpenDocument Presentation template</li>
<li>PEZ – <a href="/wiki/Prezi" title="Prezi">Prezi</a> Desktop Presentation</li>
<li>POT – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_PowerPoint" title="Microsoft PowerPoint">Microsoft PowerPoint</a> template</li>
<li>PPS – Microsoft PowerPoint Show</li>
<li>PPT – Microsoft PowerPoint Presentation</li>
<li>PPTX – <a href="/wiki/Office_Open_XML" title="Office Open XML">Office Open XML</a> Presentation</li>
<li>PRZ – <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Freelance_Graphics" class="mw-redirect" title="Lotus Freelance Graphics">Lotus Freelance Graphics</a></li>
<li>SDD – <a href="/wiki/StarOffice" title="StarOffice">StarOffice</a>'s StarImpress</li>
<li>SHF – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hancom_ThinkFree_Office&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hancom ThinkFree Office (page does not exist)">ThinkFree</a> Show</li>
<li>SHOW – Haansoft(Hancom) Presentation software document</li>
<li>SHW – <a href="/wiki/Corel_Presentations" title="Corel Presentations">Corel Presentations</a> slide show creation</li>
<li>SLP – Logix-4D Manager Show Control Project</li>
<li>SSPSS – SongShow Plus Slide Show</li>
<li>STI – <a href="/wiki/OpenOffice.org_XML" title="OpenOffice.org XML">OpenOffice.org XML</a> (obsolete) Presentation template</li>
<li>SXI – <a href="/wiki/OpenOffice.org_XML" title="OpenOffice.org XML">OpenOffice.org XML</a> (obsolete) Presentation</li>
<li>THMX – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_PowerPoint" title="Microsoft PowerPoint">Microsoft PowerPoint</a> theme template</li>
<li>WATCH – Dataton <a href="/wiki/Watchout" class="mw-redirect" title="Watchout">Watchout</a> Presentation</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Project_management_software">Project management software</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Project management software">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Project_management_software" title="Project management software">Project management software</a></div>
<ul><li>MPP – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Project" title="Microsoft Project">Microsoft Project</a></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reference_management_software">Reference management software</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Reference management software">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Reference_management_software" title="Reference management software">Reference management software</a></div>
<p>Formats of files used for bibliographic information (<a href="/wiki/Citation" title="Citation">citation</a>) management.
</p>
<ul><li>bib – <a href="/wiki/BibTeX" title="BibTeX">BibTeX</a></li>
<li>enl – <a href="/wiki/EndNote" title="EndNote">EndNote</a></li>
<li>ris – Research Information Systems <a href="/wiki/RIS_(file_format)" title="RIS (file format)">RIS (file format)</a></li></ul>
<h2><span id="Scientific_data_.28data_exchange.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_data_(data_exchange)">Scientific data (data exchange)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Scientific data (data exchange)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/FITS" title="FITS">FITS</a> (Flexible Image Transport System) – standard data format for astronomy (.fits)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Silo_(library)" title="Silo (library)">Silo</a> – a storage format for visualization developed at <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Livermore_National_Laboratory" title="Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory">Lawrence Livermore National Laboratory</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SPC_file_format" title="SPC file format">SPC</a> – spectroscopic data</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/EAS3" title="EAS3">EAS3</a> – binary format for structured data</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=EOSSA&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="EOSSA (page does not exist)">EOSSA</a> – Electro-Optic Space Situational Awareness format</li>
<li>OST (Open Spatio-Temporal) – extensible, mainly images with related data, or just pure data; meant as an open alternative for microscope images</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CCP4_(file_format)" title="CCP4 (file format)">CCP4</a> – X-ray crystallography voxels (electron density)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MRC_(file_format)" title="MRC (file format)">MRC</a> – voxels in cryo-electron microscopy</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HITRAN" title="HITRAN">HITRAN</a> – spectroscopic data with one optical/infrared transition per line in the ASCII file (.hit)</li>
<li>.root – hierarchical platform-independent compressed binary format used by <a href="/wiki/ROOT" title="ROOT">ROOT</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Simple_Data_Format" title="Simple Data Format">Simple Data Format (SDF)</a> – a platform-independent, precision-preserving binary data I/O format capable of handling large, multi-dimensional arrays.</li>
<li>MYD – Everfine LEDSpec software file for LED measurements</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multi-domain">Multi-domain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Multi-domain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/NetCDF" title="NetCDF">NetCDF</a> – Network common data format</li>
<li>HDR, [HDF], h4 or h5 – <a href="/wiki/Hierarchical_Data_Format" title="Hierarchical Data Format">Hierarchical Data Format</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SDXF" title="SDXF">SDXF</a> – (Structured Data Exchange Format)</li>
<li>CDF – <a href="/wiki/Common_Data_Format" title="Common Data Format">Common Data Format</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CGNS" title="CGNS">CGNS</a> – CFD General Notation System</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://dx.doi.org/10.1016/j.cpc.2009.11.014">FMF</a> – Full-Metadata Format</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorology">Meteorology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Meteorology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/GRIB" title="GRIB">GRIB</a> – Grid in Binary, WMO format for weather model data</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BUFR" title="BUFR">BUFR</a> – WMO format for weather observation data</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PP-format" title="PP-format">PP</a> – UK Met Office format for weather model data</li>
<li>NASA-Ames – Simple text format for observation data. First used in aircraft studies of the atmosphere.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chemistry">Chemistry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Chemistry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Chemical_file_format" title="Chemical file format">chemical file format</a></div>
<ul><li>CML – <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Markup_Language" title="Chemical Markup Language">Chemical Markup Language</a> (CML) (.cml)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chemical_table_file" title="Chemical table file">Chemical table file</a> (CTab) (.mol, .sd, .sdf)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joint_Committee_on_Atomic_and_Molecular_Physical_Data" title="Joint Committee on Atomic and Molecular Physical Data">Joint Committee on Atomic and Molecular Physical Data</a> (JCAMP) (.dx, .jdx)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Simplified_molecular_input_line_entry_specification" class="mw-redirect" title="Simplified molecular input line entry specification">Simplified molecular input line entry specification</a> (SMILES) (.smi)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mathematics">Mathematics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Mathematics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>graph6, sparse6 – ASCII encoding of <a href="/wiki/Adjacency_matrix" title="Adjacency matrix">Adjacency matrices</a> (.g6, .s6)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biology">Biology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Biology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Molecular biology and bioinformatics:
<ul><li>AB1 – In <a href="/wiki/DNA_sequencing" title="DNA sequencing">DNA sequencing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chromatogram" class="mw-redirect" title="Chromatogram">chromatogram</a> files used by instruments from <a href="/wiki/Applied_Biosystems" title="Applied Biosystems">Applied Biosystems</a></li>
<li>ACE – A <a href="/wiki/Sequence_assembly" title="Sequence assembly">sequence assembly</a> format</li>
<li>ASN.1– <a href="/wiki/Abstract_Syntax_Notation_One" title="Abstract Syntax Notation One">Abstract Syntax Notation One</a>, is an International Standards Organization (<a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardization" title="International Organization for Standardization">ISO</a>) data representation format used to achieve interoperability between platforms. <a href="/wiki/National_Center_for_Biotechnology_Information" title="National Center for Biotechnology Information">NCBI</a> uses ASN.1 for the storage and retrieval of data such as nucleotide and protein sequences, structures, genomes, and PubMed records.</li>
<li>BAM – <a href="/wiki/Binary_Alignment/Map" class="mw-redirect" title="Binary Alignment/Map">Binary Alignment/Map</a> format (compressed SAM format)</li>
<li>BCF – Binary compressed VCF format</li>
<li>BED – The <a href="/wiki/BED_file_format" class="mw-redirect" title="BED file format">browser extensible display format</a> is used for describing <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">genes</a> and other features of <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> sequences</li>
<li>CAF – Common Assembly Format for <a href="/wiki/Sequence_assembly" title="Sequence assembly">sequence assembly</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/CRAM_(file_format)" title="CRAM (file format)">CRAM</a> – compressed file format for storing biological sequences aligned to a reference sequence</li>
<li>DDBJ – The flatfile format used by the <a href="/wiki/DNA_Data_Bank_of_Japan" title="DNA Data Bank of Japan">DDBJ</a> to represent database records for <a href="/wiki/Nucleotide_sequence" class="mw-redirect" title="Nucleotide sequence">nucleotide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peptide_sequence" class="mw-redirect" title="Peptide sequence">peptide sequences</a> from <a href="/wiki/DDBJ" class="mw-redirect" title="DDBJ">DDBJ</a> databases.</li>
<li>EMBL – The flatfile format used by the <a href="/wiki/European_Molecular_Biology_Laboratory" title="European Molecular Biology Laboratory">EMBL</a> to represent database records for <a href="/wiki/Nucleotide_sequence" class="mw-redirect" title="Nucleotide sequence">nucleotide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peptide_sequence" class="mw-redirect" title="Peptide sequence">peptide sequences</a> from <a href="/wiki/EMBL" class="mw-redirect" title="EMBL">EMBL</a> databases.</li>
<li>FASTA – The <a href="/wiki/FASTA_format" title="FASTA format">FASTA format</a>, for sequence data. Sometimes also given as FNA or FAA (Fasta Nucleic Acid or Fasta Amino Acid).</li>
<li>FASTQ – The <a href="/wiki/FASTQ_format" title="FASTQ format">FASTQ format</a>, for sequence data with quality. Sometimes also given as QUAL.</li>
<li>GCPROJ – The <a href="/wiki/Genome_Compiler" class="mw-redirect" title="Genome Compiler">Genome Compiler</a> project. Advanced format for genetic data to be designed, shared and visualized.</li>
<li>GenBank – The flatfile format used by the <a href="/wiki/National_Center_for_Biotechnology_Information" title="National Center for Biotechnology Information">NCBI</a> to represent database records for <a href="/wiki/Nucleotide_sequence" class="mw-redirect" title="Nucleotide sequence">nucleotide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peptide_sequence" class="mw-redirect" title="Peptide sequence">peptide sequences</a> from the <a href="/wiki/GenBank" title="GenBank">GenBank</a> and <a href="/wiki/RefSeq" title="RefSeq">RefSeq</a> databases</li>
<li>GFF – The <a href="/wiki/General_feature_format" title="General feature format">General feature format</a> is used to describe <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">genes</a> and other features of <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a>, <a href="/wiki/RNA" title="RNA">RNA</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">protein</a> sequences</li>
<li>GTF – The <a href="/wiki/Gene_transfer_format" title="Gene transfer format">Gene transfer format</a> is used to hold information about <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">gene</a> structure</li>
<li>NCBI ASN.1 – Structured <a href="/wiki/ASN.1" class="mw-redirect" title="ASN.1">ASN.1</a> format used at <a href="/wiki/National_Center_for_Biotechnology_Information" title="National Center for Biotechnology Information">National Center for Biotechnology Information</a> for DNA and protein data</li>
<li>NEXUS – The <a href="/wiki/Nexus_file" title="Nexus file">Nexus file</a> encodes mixed information about genetic sequence data in a block structured format</li>
<li>NeXML–XML format for <a href="/wiki/Phylogenetic_tree" title="Phylogenetic tree">phylogenetic trees</a></li>
<li>NWK – The <a href="/wiki/Newick_format" title="Newick format">Newick tree format</a> is a way of representing graph-theoretical trees with edge lengths using parentheses and commas and useful to hold <a href="/wiki/Phylogenetic_tree" title="Phylogenetic tree">phylogenetic trees</a>.</li>
<li>PDB – structures of biomolecules deposited in <a href="/wiki/Protein_Data_Bank" title="Protein Data Bank">Protein Data Bank</a>, also used to exchange protein and nucleic acid structures</li>
<li>PHD – Phred output, from the basecalling software <a href="/wiki/Phred_base_calling" title="Phred base calling">Phred</a></li>
<li>PLN – Protein Line Notation used in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.biochemfusion.com/products/">proteax software</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.biochemfusion.com/doc/Biochemfusion_PLN_1.4_spec.pdf">specification</a></li>
<li>SAM – <a href="/wiki/Sequence_Alignment/Map" class="mw-redirect" title="Sequence Alignment/Map">Sequence Alignment/Map</a> format, in which the results of the <a href="/wiki/1000_Genomes_Project" title="1000 Genomes Project">1000 Genomes Project</a> will be released</li>
<li>SBML – <a href="/wiki/SBML" title="SBML">The Systems Biology Markup Language</a> is used to store biochemical network computational models</li>
<li>SCF – Staden chromatogram files used to store data from <a href="/wiki/DNA_sequencing" title="DNA sequencing">DNA sequencing</a></li>
<li>SFF – <a href="/wiki/Standard_Flowgram_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Flowgram Format">Standard Flowgram Format</a></li>
<li>SRA – format used by the <a href="/wiki/National_Center_for_Biotechnology_Information" title="National Center for Biotechnology Information">National Center for Biotechnology Information</a> Short Read Archive to store high-throughput DNA sequence data</li>
<li>Stockholm – The <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_format" title="Stockholm format">Stockholm format</a> for representing <a href="/wiki/Multiple_sequence_alignment" title="Multiple sequence alignment">multiple sequence alignments</a></li>
<li>Swiss-Prot – The flatfile format used to represent database records for <a href="/wiki/Peptide_sequence" class="mw-redirect" title="Peptide sequence">protein</a> sequences from the <a href="/wiki/Swiss-Prot" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss-Prot">Swiss-Prot</a> database</li>
<li>VCF – <a href="/wiki/Variant_Call_Format" title="Variant Call Format">Variant Call Format</a>, a standard created by the <a href="/wiki/1000_Genomes_Project" title="1000 Genomes Project">1000 Genomes Project</a> that lists and annotates the entire collection of human variants (with the exception of approximately 1.6 million variants).</li></ul></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biomedical_imaging">Biomedical imaging</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Biomedical imaging">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Digital_Imaging_and_Communications_in_Medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="Digital Imaging and Communications in Medicine">Digital Imaging and Communications in Medicine</a> (DICOM) (.dcm)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neuroimaging_Informatics_Technology_Initiative" title="Neuroimaging Informatics Technology Initiative">Neuroimaging Informatics Technology Initiative</a> (NIfTI)
<ul><li>.nii – single-file (combined data and meta-data) style
<ul><li>.nii.gz – <a href="/wiki/Gzip" title="Gzip">gzip</a>-compressed, used transparently by some software, notably the <a href="/wiki/FMRIB_Software_Library" title="FMRIB Software Library">FMRIB Software Library</a> (FSL)</li>
<li>.gii – single-file (combined data and meta-data) style; NIfTI offspring for brain surface data</li></ul></li>
<li>.img,.hdr – dual-file (separate data and meta-data, respectively) style</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Afni" class="mw-redirect" title="Afni">AFNI</a> data, meta-data (.BRIK,.HEAD)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_General_Hospital" title="Massachusetts General Hospital">Massachusetts General Hospital</a> imaging format, used by the <a href="/wiki/FreeSurfer" title="FreeSurfer">FreeSurfer</a> brain analysis package
<ul><li>.MGH – uncompressed</li>
<li>.MGZ – <a href="/wiki/ZIP_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="ZIP (file format)">zip</a>-compressed</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Analyze_(imaging_software)" title="Analyze (imaging software)">Analyze</a> data, meta-data (.img,.hdr)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Medical_Imaging_NetCDF&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Medical Imaging NetCDF (page does not exist)">Medical Imaging NetCDF</a> (MINC) format, previously based on NetCDF; since version 2.0, based on HDF5 (.mnc)</li></ul>
<h3><span id="Biomedical_signals_.28time_series.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Biomedical_signals_(time_series)">Biomedical signals (time series)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Biomedical signals (time series)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>ACQ – AcqKnowledge format for Windows/PC from Biopac Systems Inc., Goleta, CA, USA</li>
<li>ADICHT – LabChart format from ADInstruments Pty Ltd, Bella Vista NSW, Australia</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BCI2000" title="BCI2000">BCI2000</a> – The <a href="/wiki/BCI2000" title="BCI2000">BCI2000</a> project, Albany, NY, USA</li>
<li>BDF – BioSemi data format from BioSemi B.V. Amsterdam, Netherlands</li>
<li>BKR – The EEG data format developed at the University of Technology Graz, Austria</li>
<li>CFWB – Chart Data Format from ADInstruments Pty Ltd, Bella Vista NSW, Australia</li>
<li>DICOM – Waveform An extension of Dicom for storing waveform data</li>
<li>ecgML – A markup language for electrocardiogram data acquisition and analysis</li>
<li>EDF/EDF+ – European Data Format</li>
<li>FEF – File Exchange Format for Vital signs, CEN TS 14271</li>
<li>GDF v1.x – The General Data Format for biomedical signals, version 1.x</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://arxiv.org/pdf/cs/0608052">GDF</a> v2.x – The General Data Format for biomedical signals, version 2.x</li>
<li>HL7aECG – Health Level 7 v3 annotated ECG</li>
<li>MFER – Medical waveform Format Encoding Rules</li>
<li>OpenXDF – Open Exchange Data Format from Neurotronics, Inc., Gainesville, FL, USA</li>
<li>SCP-ECG – Standard Communication Protocol for Computer assisted electrocardiography EN1064:2007</li>
<li>SIGIF – A digital SIGnal Interchange Format with application in neurophysiology</li>
<li>WFDB – Format of Physiobank</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://code.google.com/p/xdf/">XDF</a> – eXtensible Data Format</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_biomedical_formats">Other biomedical formats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Other biomedical formats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Health_Level_7" title="Health Level 7">Health Level 7</a> (HL7) – a framework for exchange, integration, sharing, and retrieval of health information electronically</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/XDT" title="XDT">xDT</a> – a family of data exchange formats for medical records</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biometric_formats">Biometric formats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Biometric formats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=CBF_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="CBF (file format) (page does not exist)">CBF</a> – Common Biometric Format, based on CBEFF 2.0 (Common Biometric ExFramework).</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=EBF_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="EBF (file format) (page does not exist)">EBF</a> – Extended Biometric Format, based on CBF but with S/MIME encryption support and semantic extensions</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=CBFX_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="CBFX (file format) (page does not exist)">CBFX</a> – XML Common Biometric Format, based upon XCBF 1.1 (OASIS XML Common Biometric Format)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=EBFX&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="EBFX (page does not exist)">EBFX</a> – XML Extended Biometric Format, based on CBFX but with W3C XML Encryption support and semantic extensions</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Programming_languages_and_scripts"><span id="Script"></span><span id="Programming_languages_and_scripts">Programming languages and scripts</span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Programming languages and scripts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>ADB – <a href="/wiki/Ada_(programming_language)" title="Ada (programming language)">Ada</a> body</li>
<li>ADS – <a href="/wiki/Ada_(programming_language)" title="Ada (programming language)">Ada</a> specification</li>
<li>AHK – <a href="/wiki/AutoHotkey" title="AutoHotkey">AutoHotkey</a> script file</li>
<li>APPLESCRIPT- <a href="/wiki/Applescript" class="mw-redirect" title="Applescript">applescript</a> – see SCPT</li>
<li>AS – <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash" title="Adobe Flash">Adobe Flash</a> <a href="/wiki/ActionScript" title="ActionScript">ActionScript</a> File</li>
<li>AU3 – <a href="/wiki/AutoIt" title="AutoIt">AutoIt version 3</a></li>
<li>BAT – <a href="/wiki/Batch_file" title="Batch file">Batch file</a></li>
<li>BAS – <a href="/wiki/QBasic" title="QBasic">QBasic</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/QuickBASIC" title="QuickBASIC">QuickBASIC</a></li>
<li>CLJS – <a href="/wiki/ClojureScript" class="mw-redirect" title="ClojureScript">ClojureScript</a></li>
<li>CMD – <a href="/wiki/Batch_file" title="Batch file">Batch file</a></li>
<li>Coffee – <a href="/wiki/CoffeeScript" title="CoffeeScript">CoffeeScript</a></li>
<li>C – <a href="/wiki/The_C_Programming_Language" title="The C Programming Language">C</a></li>
<li>CPP – <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a></li>
<li>INO – <a href="/wiki/Arduino" title="Arduino">Arduino</a> sketch (program)</li>
<li>EGG – <a href="/wiki/Chicken_Scheme_compiler" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicken Scheme compiler">Chicken</a></li>
<li>EGT – EGT Asterisk Application Source File, EGT Universal Document</li>
<li>ERB – <a href="/wiki/Embedded_Ruby" class="mw-redirect" title="Embedded Ruby">Embedded Ruby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruby_on_Rails" title="Ruby on Rails">Ruby on Rails</a> Script File</li>
<li>HTA – <a href="/wiki/HTA_(programming_language)" class="mw-redirect" title="HTA (programming language)">HTML Application</a></li>
<li>IBI – Icarus script</li>
<li>ICI – <a href="/wiki/ICI_(programming_language)" title="ICI (programming language)">ICI</a></li>
<li>IJS – <a href="/wiki/J_(programming_language)" title="J (programming language)">J</a> script</li>
<li>.ipynb – <a href="/wiki/IPython" title="IPython">IPython</a> Notebook</li>
<li>ITCL – <a href="/wiki/Itcl" class="mw-redirect" title="Itcl">Itcl</a></li>
<li>JS – <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a> and <a href="/wiki/JScript" title="JScript">JScript</a></li>
<li>JSFL – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Adobe_JavaScript_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Adobe JavaScript language (page does not exist)">Adobe JavaScript language</a></li>
<li>LUA – <a href="/wiki/Lua_programming_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Lua programming language">Lua</a></li>
<li>M – <a href="/wiki/Mathematica" class="mw-redirect" title="Mathematica">Mathematica</a> package file</li>
<li>MRC – <a href="/wiki/MIRC_script" class="mw-redirect" title="MIRC script">mIRC Script</a></li>
<li>NCF – <a href="/wiki/NetWare" title="NetWare">NetWare</a> Command File (scripting for Novell's NetWare OS)</li>
<li>NUC – compiled script</li>
<li>NUD – <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a> External module written in C++</li>
<li>NUT – <a href="/wiki/Squirrel_programming_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Squirrel programming language">Squirrel</a></li>
<li>pde – <a href="/wiki/Processing_(programming_language)" title="Processing (programming language)">Processing (programming language)</a>, Processing script</li>
<li>PHP – <a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">PHP</a></li>
<li>PHP? – <a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">PHP</a> (? = version number)</li>
<li>PL – <a href="/wiki/Perl" title="Perl">Perl</a></li>
<li>PM – <a href="/wiki/Perl_module" title="Perl module">Perl module</a></li>
<li>PS1 – <a href="/wiki/Windows_PowerShell" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows PowerShell">Windows PowerShell</a> shell script</li>
<li>PS1XML – <a href="/wiki/Windows_PowerShell" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows PowerShell">Windows PowerShell</a> format and type definitions</li>
<li>PSC1 – <a href="/wiki/Windows_PowerShell" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows PowerShell">Windows PowerShell</a> console file</li>
<li>PSD1 – <a href="/wiki/Windows_PowerShell" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows PowerShell">Windows PowerShell</a> data file</li>
<li>PSM1 – <a href="/wiki/Windows_PowerShell" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows PowerShell">Windows PowerShell</a> module file</li>
<li>PY – <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a></li>
<li>PYC – <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a> byte code files</li>
<li>PYO – <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a></li>
<li>R – <a href="/wiki/R_(programming_language)" title="R (programming language)">R scripts</a></li>
<li>r – <a href="/wiki/REBOL" class="mw-redirect" title="REBOL">REBOL scripts</a></li>
<li>RB – <a href="/wiki/Ruby_programming_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruby programming language">Ruby</a></li>
<li>RDP – <a href="/wiki/Remote_Desktop_Protocol" title="Remote Desktop Protocol">RDP</a> connection</li>
<li>red – <a href="/wiki/Red_(programming_language)" title="Red (programming language)">Red scripts</a></li>
<li>RS – <a href="/wiki/Rust_(programming_language)" title="Rust (programming language)">Rust (programming language)</a></li>
<li>SB2 – <a href="/wiki/Scratch_(programming_language)" title="Scratch (programming language)">Scratch</a></li>
<li>SCPT – <a href="/wiki/Applescript" class="mw-redirect" title="Applescript">Applescript</a></li>
<li>SCPTD – See SCPT.</li>
<li>SDL – <a href="/w/index.php?title=State_Description_Language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="State Description Language (page does not exist)">State Description Language</a></li>
<li>SH – <a href="/wiki/Shell_script" title="Shell script">Shell script</a></li>
<li>SYJS – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://symatapp.com">SyMAT</a> JavaScript</li>
<li>SYPY – SyMAT Python</li>
<li>TCL – <a href="/wiki/Tcl" title="Tcl">Tcl</a></li>
<li>TNS – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://fileinfo.com/extension/tns">Ti-Nspire Code/File</a></li>
<li>VBS – <a href="/wiki/VBScript" title="VBScript">Visual Basic Script</a></li>
<li>XPL – <a href="/wiki/XProc" title="XProc">XProc</a> script/pipeline</li>
<li>ebuild – <a href="/wiki/Gentoo_linux" class="mw-redirect" title="Gentoo linux">Gentoo linux</a>'s portage package.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Authentication and general encryption formats are listed here.
</p>
<ul><li>OpenPGP Message Format – used by <a href="/wiki/Pretty_Good_Privacy" title="Pretty Good Privacy">Pretty Good Privacy</a>, <a href="/wiki/GNU_Privacy_Guard" title="GNU Privacy Guard">GNU Privacy Guard</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/OpenPGP" class="mw-redirect" title="OpenPGP">OpenPGP</a> software; can contain keys, signed data, or encrypted data; can be binary or text ("<a href="/wiki/ASCII_armor" class="mw-redirect" title="ASCII armor">ASCII armored</a>")</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Certificates_and_keys">Certificates and keys</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Certificates and keys">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>GXK – Galaxkey, an encryption platform for authorized, private and confidential email communication<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OpenSSH" title="OpenSSH">OpenSSH</a> private key (.ssh) – <a href="/wiki/Secure_Shell" title="Secure Shell">Secure Shell</a> <a href="/wiki/Private_key" class="mw-redirect" title="Private key">private key</a>; format generated by <a href="/wiki/Ssh-keygen" title="Ssh-keygen">ssh-keygen</a> or converted from PPK with <a href="/wiki/PuTTYgen" class="mw-redirect" title="PuTTYgen">PuTTYgen</a><sup id="cite_ref-wipo_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wipo-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leading_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leading-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leo_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leo-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/OpenSSH" title="OpenSSH">OpenSSH</a> public key (.pub) – <a href="/wiki/Secure_Shell" title="Secure Shell">Secure Shell</a> <a href="/wiki/Public_key" class="mw-redirect" title="Public key">public key</a>; format generated by <a href="/wiki/Ssh-keygen" title="Ssh-keygen">ssh-keygen</a> or <a href="/wiki/PuTTY" title="PuTTY">PuTTYgen</a><sup id="cite_ref-wipo_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wipo-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leading_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leading-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leo_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leo-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PuTTY" title="PuTTY">PuTTY</a> private key (.ppk) – <a href="/wiki/Secure_Shell" title="Secure Shell">Secure Shell</a> <a href="/wiki/Private_key" class="mw-redirect" title="Private key">private key</a>, in the format generated by <a href="/wiki/PuTTY" title="PuTTY">PuTTYgen</a> instead of the format used by <a href="/wiki/OpenSSH" title="OpenSSH">OpenSSH</a><sup id="cite_ref-wipo_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wipo-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leading_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leading-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leo_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leo-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="X.509"><a href="/wiki/X.509" title="X.509">X.509</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: X.509">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Distinguished_Encoding_Rules" class="mw-redirect" title="Distinguished Encoding Rules">Distinguished Encoding Rules</a> (.cer, .crt, .der) – stores certificates</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PKCS7" class="mw-redirect" title="PKCS7">PKCS#7</a> SignedData (.p7b, .p7c) – commonly appears without main data, just certificates or <a href="/wiki/Revocation_list" class="mw-redirect" title="Revocation list">certificate revocation lists</a> (CRLs)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PKCS_12" title="PKCS 12">PKCS#12</a> (.p12, .pfx) – can store public certificates and private keys</li>
<li>PEM – <a href="/wiki/Privacy-enhanced_Electronic_Mail" class="mw-redirect" title="Privacy-enhanced Electronic Mail">Privacy-enhanced Electronic Mail</a>: full format not widely used, but often used to store <a href="/wiki/Distinguished_Encoding_Rules" class="mw-redirect" title="Distinguished Encoding Rules">Distinguished Encoding Rules</a> in <a href="/wiki/Base64" title="Base64">Base64</a> format</li>
<li>PFX – Microsoft predecessor of PKCS#12</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Encrypted_files">Encrypted files</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Encrypted files">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This section shows file formats for encrypted general data, rather than a specific program's data.
</p>
<ul><li>AXX – Encrypted file, created with <a href="/wiki/AxCrypt" title="AxCrypt">AxCrypt</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Encrypted_Email_Attachment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Encrypted Email Attachment (page does not exist)">EEA</a> – An encrypted CAB, ostensibly for protecting email attachments</li>
<li>TC – Virtual encrypted disk container, created by <a href="/wiki/TrueCrypt" title="TrueCrypt">TrueCrypt</a></li>
<li>KODE – Encrypted file, created with KodeFile</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Password_files">Password files</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Password files">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Password" title="Password">Password</a> files (sometimes called keychain files) contain lists of other passwords, usually encrypted.
</p>
<ul><li>BPW – Encrypted password file created by Bitser password manager</li>
<li>KDB – <a href="/wiki/KeePass" title="KeePass">KeePass</a> 1 database</li>
<li>KDBX – <a href="/wiki/KeePass" title="KeePass">KeePass</a> 2 database</li></ul>
<h2><span id="Signal_data_.28non-audio.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Signal_data_(non-audio)">Signal data (non-audio)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Signal data (non-audio)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>ACQ – AcqKnowledge format for Windows/PC from Biopac</li>
<li>ADICHT – LabChart format from ADInstruments</li>
<li>BKR – The EEG data format developed at the University of Technology Graz</li>
<li>BDF, CFG – Configuration file for <a href="/wiki/Comtrade" title="Comtrade">Comtrade</a> data</li>
<li>CFWB – Chart Data format from <a href="/wiki/ADInstruments" title="ADInstruments">ADInstruments</a></li>
<li>DAT – Raw data file for <a href="/wiki/Comtrade" title="Comtrade">Comtrade</a> data</li>
<li>EDF – European data format</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=FEF_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="FEF (file format) (page does not exist)">FEF</a> – File Exchange Format for Vital signs</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/General_Data_Format_for_Biomedical_Signals" title="General Data Format for Biomedical Signals">GDF</a> – General data formats for biomedical signals</li>
<li>GMS – Gesture And Motion Signal format</li>
<li>IROCK – intelliRock Sensor Data File Format</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=MFER&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="MFER (page does not exist)">MFER</a> – Medical waveform Format Encoding Rules</li>
<li>SAC – Seismic Analysis Code, earthquake seismology data format<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SCP-ECG" title="SCP-ECG">SCP-ECG</a> – Standard Communication Protocol for Computer assisted electrocardiography</li>
<li>SEED, MSEED – Standard for the Exchange of Earthquake Data, seismological data and sensor metadata<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SEG_Y" class="mw-redirect" title="SEG Y">SEGY</a> – <a href="/wiki/Reflection_seismology" title="Reflection seismology">Reflection seismology</a> data format</li>
<li>SIGIF – SIGnal Interchange Format</li>
<li>WIN, WIN32 – NIED/ERI seismic data format (.cnt)<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sound_and_music">Sound and music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Sound and music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lossless_audio"><a href="/wiki/Audio_compression_(data)#Difficulties_in_lossless_compression_of_audio_data" class="mw-redirect" title="Audio compression (data)">Lossless</a> audio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Lossless audio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Uncompressed">Uncompressed</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Uncompressed">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/8SVX" title="8SVX">8SVX</a> – Commodore-Amiga 8-bit sound (usually in an <a href="/wiki/Interchange_File_Format" title="Interchange File Format">IFF</a> container)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/8SVX" title="8SVX">16SVX</a> – Commodore-Amiga 16-bit sound (usually in an <a href="/wiki/Interchange_File_Format" title="Interchange File Format">IFF</a> container)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AIFF" class="mw-redirect" title="AIFF">AIFF</a>, AIF, AIFC – Audio Interchange File Format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Au_file_format" title="Au file format">AU</a> – Simple <a href="/wiki/Audio_file_format" title="Audio file format">audio file format</a> introduced by <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Broadcast_Wave_Format" title="Broadcast Wave Format">BWF</a> – Broadcast Wave Format, an extension of WAVE</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Red_Book_(audio_CD_standard)" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Book (audio CD standard)">CDDA</a> – Compact Disc Digital Audio</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Raw_audio_format" title="Raw audio format">RAW</a> – Raw samples without any header or sync</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WAV" title="WAV">WAV</a> – Microsoft Wave</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Compressed">Compressed</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Compressed">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>RA, RM – <a href="/wiki/RealAudio" title="RealAudio">RealAudio</a> format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/FLAC" title="FLAC">FLAC</a> – <a href="/wiki/Libre_software" class="mw-redirect" title="Libre software">Free</a> lossless codec of the <a href="/wiki/Ogg" title="Ogg">Ogg</a> project</li>
<li>LA – <a href="/wiki/Lossless_Audio" class="mw-redirect" title="Lossless Audio">Lossless Audio</a></li>
<li>PAC – <a href="/wiki/Lossless_Predictive_Audio_Compression" class="mw-redirect" title="Lossless Predictive Audio Compression">LPAC</a></li>
<li>APE – <a href="/wiki/Monkey%27s_Audio" title="Monkey&#39;s Audio">Monkey's Audio</a></li>
<li>OFR, OFS, OFF – <a href="/wiki/OptimFROG" title="OptimFROG">OptimFROG</a></li>
<li>RKA – RKAU</li>
<li>SHN – <a href="/wiki/Shorten_(file_format)" title="Shorten (file format)">Shorten</a></li>
<li>TAK – Tom's Lossless Audio Kompressor<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>THD – <a href="/wiki/Dolby_TrueHD" title="Dolby TrueHD">Dolby TrueHD</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TTA_(codec)" title="TTA (codec)">TTA</a> – Free lossless audio codec (True Audio)</li>
<li>WV – <a href="/wiki/WavPack" title="WavPack">WavPack</a></li>
<li>WMA – <a href="/wiki/Windows_Media_Audio" title="Windows Media Audio">Windows Media Audio</a> 9 Lossless</li>
<li>BRSTM – Binary Revolution Stream<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>DTS, DTSHD, DTSMA – <a href="/wiki/DTS_(sound_system)" title="DTS (sound system)">DTS (sound system)</a></li>
<li>AST – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> Audio Stream<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>AW – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> Audio Sample used in first-party games</li>
<li>PSF – <a href="/wiki/Portable_Sound_Format" title="Portable Sound Format">Portable Sound Format</a>, PlayStation variant (originally PlayStation Sound Format)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lossy_audio"><a href="/wiki/Audio_data_compression#Lossy_compression" class="mw-redirect" title="Audio data compression">Lossy</a> audio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Lossy audio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dolby_AC3" class="mw-redirect" title="Dolby AC3">AC3</a> – Usually used for <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Digital" title="Dolby Digital">Dolby Digital</a> tracks</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adaptive_Multi-Rate_audio_codec" title="Adaptive Multi-Rate audio codec">AMR</a> – For <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">GSM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Universal_Mobile_Telecommunications_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Mobile Telecommunications System">UMTS</a> based mobile phones</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MP1" class="mw-redirect" title="MP1">MP1</a> – <a href="/wiki/Moving_Picture_Experts_Group" title="Moving Picture Experts Group">MPEG</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mpeg.chiariglione.org/standards/mpeg-1/audio">Layer 1</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MP2_(format)" class="mw-redirect" title="MP2 (format)">MP2</a> – <a href="/wiki/Moving_Picture_Experts_Group" title="Moving Picture Experts Group">MPEG</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mpeg.chiariglione.org/standards/mpeg-1/audio">Layer 2</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MP3" title="MP3">MP3</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Moving_Picture_Experts_Group" title="Moving Picture Experts Group">MPEG</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://mpeg.chiariglione.org/standards/mpeg-1/audio">Layer 3</a></li>
<li>SPX – <a href="/wiki/Speex" title="Speex">Speex</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ogg" title="Ogg">Ogg</a> project, specialized for voice, low bitrates)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">GSM</a> – GSM <a href="/wiki/Full_Rate" title="Full Rate">Full Rate</a>, originally developed for use in mobile phones</li>
<li>WMA – <a href="/wiki/Windows_Media_Audio" title="Windows Media Audio">Windows Media Audio</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Advanced_Audio_Coding" title="Advanced Audio Coding">AAC</a> – Advanced Audio Coding (usually in an <a href="/wiki/MPEG-4" title="MPEG-4">MPEG-4</a> container)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Musepack" title="Musepack">MPC</a> – Musepack</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/TwinVQ" title="TwinVQ">VQF</a> – Yamaha TwinVQ</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=OTS_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="OTS (file format) (page does not exist)">OTS</a> – Audio File (similar to MP3, with more data stored in the file and slightly better compression; designed for use with <a href="/w/index.php?title=OtsLabs&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="OtsLabs (page does not exist)">OtsLabs</a>' <a href="/w/index.php?title=OtsAV&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="OtsAV (page does not exist)">OtsAV</a>)</li>
<li>SWA – <a href="/wiki/Macromedia_Shockwave" class="mw-redirect" title="Macromedia Shockwave">Macromedia Shockwave</a> Audio (Same compression as <a href="/wiki/MP3" title="MP3">MP3</a> with additional header information specific to <a href="/wiki/Macromedia_Director" class="mw-redirect" title="Macromedia Director">Macromedia Director</a></li>
<li>VOX – <a href="/wiki/Dialogic_ADPCM" title="Dialogic ADPCM">Dialogic ADPCM</a> Low Sample Rate Digitized Voice</li>
<li>VOC – <a href="/wiki/Creative_Labs" class="mw-redirect" title="Creative Labs">Creative Labs</a> <a href="/wiki/Soundblaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Soundblaster">Soundblaster</a> Creative Voice 8-bit &amp; 16-bit Also output format of RCA Audio Recorders</li>
<li>DWD – DiamondWare Digitized</li>
<li>SMP – Turtlebeach SampleVision</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ogg" title="Ogg">OGG</a> – Ogg Vorbis</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tracker_modules_and_related"><a href="/wiki/Tracker_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Tracker music">Tracker</a> modules and related</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Tracker modules and related">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/MOD_(file_format)" title="MOD (file format)">MOD</a> – Soundtracker and Protracker sample and melody modules</li>
<li>MT2 – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.madtracker.org/about.php">MadTracker</a> 2 module</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/S3M_(file_format)" title="S3M (file format)">S3M</a> – <a href="/wiki/Scream_Tracker" title="Scream Tracker">Scream Tracker</a> 3 module</li>
