<li><a href="/wiki/XM_(file_format)" title="XM (file format)">XM</a> – <a href="/wiki/Fast_Tracker" class="mw-redirect" title="Fast Tracker">Fast Tracker</a> module</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/IT_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="IT (file format)">IT</a> – <a href="/wiki/Impulse_Tracker" title="Impulse Tracker">Impulse Tracker</a> module</li>
<li>NSF – <a href="/wiki/NES_Sound_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="NES Sound Format">NES Sound Format</a></li>
<li>MID, MIDI – Standard <a href="/wiki/Musical_Instrument_Digital_Interface" class="mw-redirect" title="Musical Instrument Digital Interface">MIDI</a> file; most often just notes and controls but occasionally also sample dumps</li>
<li>FTM – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.famitracker.com/wiki/index.php?title=Main_Page">FamiTracker</a> Project file</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sheet_music_files">Sheet music files</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Sheet music files">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>LY – <a href="/wiki/GNU_LilyPond" class="mw-redirect" title="GNU LilyPond">LilyPond</a> sheet music file</li>
<li>MUS, MUSX – <a href="/wiki/Finale_(software)" title="Finale (software)">Finale</a> sheet music file</li>
<li>MXL, XML – <a href="/wiki/MusicXML" title="MusicXML">MusicXML</a> standard sheet music exchange format</li>
<li>MSCX, MSCZ – <a href="/wiki/MuseScore" title="MuseScore">MuseScore</a> sheet music file</li>
<li>SIB – <a href="/wiki/Sibelius_(computer_program)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sibelius (computer program)">Sibelius</a> sheet music file</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_file_formats_pertaining_to_audio">Other file formats pertaining to audio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Other file formats pertaining to audio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>NIFF – <a href="/wiki/Notation_Interchange_File_Format" title="Notation Interchange File Format">Notation Interchange File Format</a></li>
<li>PTB – <a href="/wiki/Power_Tab_Editor" title="Power Tab Editor">Power Tab Editor</a> <a href="/wiki/Tablature" title="Tablature">tab</a></li>
<li>ASF – <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Systems_Format" title="Advanced Systems Format">Advanced Systems Format</a></li>
<li>CUST – DeliPlayer custom sound format</li>
<li>GYM – <a href="/wiki/Sega_Genesis" title="Sega Genesis">Genesis</a> <a href="/wiki/YM2612" class="mw-redirect" title="YM2612">YM2612</a> log</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JAM_notation" title="JAM notation">JAM</a> – <a href="/wiki/JAM_notation" title="JAM notation">Jam music format</a></li>
<li>MNG – Background music for the <a href="/wiki/Creatures_(artificial_life_program)" class="mw-redirect" title="Creatures (artificial life program)">Creatures</a> game series, starting from Creatures 2</li>
<li>RMJ – RealJukebox Media used for <a href="/wiki/RealPlayer" title="RealPlayer">RealPlayer</a></li>
<li>SID – <a href="/wiki/MOS_Technology_SID#Software_emulation" class="mw-redirect" title="MOS Technology SID">Sound Interface Device</a> – Commodore 64 instructions to play SID music and sound effects</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=SPC700_sound_format&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="SPC700 sound format (page does not exist)">SPC</a> – <a href="/wiki/Super_Nintendo_Entertainment_System" title="Super Nintendo Entertainment System">Super NES</a> sound format</li>
<li>TXM – Track ax media</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/VGM_(file_format)" title="VGM (file format)">VGM</a> – Stands for "Video Game Music", log for several different chips</li>
<li>YM – Atari ST/Amstrad CPC <a href="/wiki/YM2149" class="mw-redirect" title="YM2149">YM2149</a> sound chip format</li>
<li>PVD – Portable Voice Document used for Oaisys &amp; Mitel call recordings</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Playlist_formats">Playlist formats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Playlist formats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li>XSPF – <a href="/wiki/XML_Shareable_Playlist_Format" title="XML Shareable Playlist Format">XML Shareable Playlist Format</a></li>
<li>ZPL – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Xbox_Music_(Formerly_Zune)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Xbox Music (Formerly Zune) (page does not exist)">Xbox Music (Formerly Zune)</a> Playlist format from Microsoft</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/PLS_(file_format)" title="PLS (file format)">PLS</a> – Multimedia <a href="/wiki/Playlist" title="Playlist">playlist</a>, originally developed for use with the museArc</li></ul>

<ul><li>ALS – <a href="/wiki/Ableton_Live" title="Ableton Live">Ableton Live</a> set</li>

<li>LOGIC – <a href="/wiki/Logic_Pro_X" class="mw-redirect" title="Logic Pro X">Logic Pro X</a> project file</li>

<li>RIN – Soundways RIN-M file containing sound recording participant credits and song information</li>
<li>SES – <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Audition" title="Adobe Audition">Adobe Audition</a> multitrack session file</li>
<li>SFL – <a href="/wiki/Sound_Forge" title="Sound Forge">Sound Forge</a> sound file</li>
<li>SNG – <a href="/wiki/MIDI" title="MIDI">MIDI</a> sequence file (<a href="/w/index.php?title=MidiSoft&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="MidiSoft (page does not exist)">MidiSoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korg" title="Korg">Korg</a>, etc.) or <a href="/wiki/N-Track_Studio" title="N-Track Studio">n-Track Studio</a> project file</li>
<li>STF – <a href="/w/index.php?title=StudioFactory&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="StudioFactory (page does not exist)">StudioFactory</a> project file. It contains all necessary patches, samples, tracks and settings to play the file</li>
<li>SND – <a href="/wiki/Akai_MPC" title="Akai MPC">Akai MPC</a> sound file</li>
<li>SYN – <a href="/wiki/SynFactory" title="SynFactory">SynFactory</a> project file. It contains all necessary patches, samples, tracks and settings to play the file</li>
<li>VCLS – VocaListener project file</li>
<li>VSQ – <a href="/wiki/Vocaloid" title="Vocaloid">Vocaloid</a> 2 Editor sequence excluding <a href="/wiki/WAV" title="WAV">wave</a>-file</li>
<li>VSQX – <a href="/wiki/Vocaloid" title="Vocaloid">Vocaloid</a> 3 Editor sequence excluding <a href="/wiki/WAV" title="WAV">wave</a>-file</li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Spreadsheet">Spreadsheet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Spreadsheet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>123 – <a href="/wiki/Lotus_1-2-3" title="Lotus 1-2-3">Lotus 1-2-3</a></li>

<li>ODS – <a href="/wiki/OpenDocument" title="OpenDocument">OpenDocument</a> spreadsheet</li>
<li>OTS – <a href="/wiki/OpenDocument" title="OpenDocument">OpenDocument</a> spreadsheet template</li>
<li>QPW – <a href="/wiki/Quattro_Pro" title="Quattro Pro">Quattro Pro</a> spreadsheet</li>
<li>SDC – <a href="/wiki/StarOffice" title="StarOffice">StarOffice</a> StarCalc Spreadsheet</li>
<li>SLK – <a href="/wiki/SYLK" class="mw-redirect" title="SYLK">SYLK</a> (SYmbolic LinK)</li>
<li>STC – <a href="/wiki/OpenOffice.org_XML" title="OpenOffice.org XML">OpenOffice.org XML</a> (obsolete) Spreadsheet template</li>
<li>SXC – <a href="/wiki/OpenOffice.org_XML" title="OpenOffice.org XML">OpenOffice.org XML</a> (obsolete) Spreadsheet</li>
<li>TAB – tab delimited columns; also TSV (<a href="/wiki/Tab-separated_values" title="Tab-separated values">Tab-Separated Values</a>)</li>
<li>TXT – text file</li>
<li>VC – Visicalc</li>
<li>WK1 – <a href="/wiki/Lotus_1-2-3" title="Lotus 1-2-3">Lotus 1-2-3</a> up to version 2.01</li>
<li>WK3 – <a href="/wiki/Lotus_1-2-3" title="Lotus 1-2-3">Lotus 1-2-3</a> version 3.0</li>
<li>WK4 – <a href="/wiki/Lotus_1-2-3" title="Lotus 1-2-3">Lotus 1-2-3</a> version 4.0</li>
<li>WKS – <a href="/wiki/Lotus_1-2-3" title="Lotus 1-2-3">Lotus 1-2-3</a></li>
<li>WKS – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Works" title="Microsoft Works">Microsoft Works</a></li>
<li>WQ1 – <a href="/wiki/Quattro_Pro" title="Quattro Pro">Quattro Pro</a> DOS version</li>
<li>XLK – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Excel" title="Microsoft Excel">Microsoft Excel</a> worksheet backup</li>
<li>XLS – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Excel" title="Microsoft Excel">Microsoft Excel</a> worksheet sheet (97–2003)</li>
<li>XLSB – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Excel" title="Microsoft Excel">Microsoft Excel</a> binary workbook</li>
<li>XLSM – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Excel" title="Microsoft Excel">Microsoft Excel</a> Macro-enabled workbook</li>
<li>XLSX – <a href="/wiki/Office_Open_XML" title="Office Open XML">Office Open XML</a> worksheet sheet</li>
<li>XLR – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Works" title="Microsoft Works">Microsoft Works</a> version 6.0</li>
<li>XLT – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Excel" title="Microsoft Excel">Microsoft Excel</a> worksheet template</li>
<li>XLTM – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Excel" title="Microsoft Excel">Microsoft Excel</a> Macro-enabled worksheet template</li>
<li>XLW – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Excel" title="Microsoft Excel">Microsoft Excel</a> worksheet workspace (version 4.0)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tabulated_data">Tabulated data</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Tabulated data">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>TSV – <a href="/wiki/Tab-separated_values" title="Tab-separated values">Tab-separated values</a></li>
<li>CSV – <a href="/wiki/Comma-separated_values" title="Comma-separated values">Comma-separated values</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Databank_format" title="Databank format">db</a> – databank format; accessible by many <a href="/wiki/Econometrics" title="Econometrics">econometric</a> applications</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Data_Interchange_Format" title="Data Interchange Format">dif</a> – accessible by many <a href="/wiki/Spreadsheet" title="Spreadsheet">spreadsheet</a> applications</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Video">Video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Video_file_format" title="Video file format">video file format</a></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Advanced_Authoring_Format" title="Advanced Authoring Format">AAF</a> – mostly intended to hold edit decisions and rendering information, but can also contain compressed media essence</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/3GP" class="mw-redirect" title="3GP">3GP</a> – the most common video format for <a href="/wiki/Cell_phones" class="mw-redirect" title="Cell phones">cell phones</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Graphics_Interchange_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Graphics Interchange Format">GIF</a> – Animated GIF (simple animation; until recently often avoided because of patent problems)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Advanced_Systems_Format" title="Advanced Systems Format">ASF</a> – container (enables any form of <a href="/wiki/Video_compression" class="mw-redirect" title="Video compression">compression</a> to be used; <a href="/wiki/MPEG-4" title="MPEG-4">MPEG-4</a> is common; video in ASF-containers is also called <a href="/wiki/Windows_Media_Video" title="Windows Media Video">Windows Media Video</a> (WMV))</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Advanced_Video_Codec_High_Definition" class="mw-redirect" title="Advanced Video Codec High Definition">AVCHD</a> – Advanced Video Codec High Definition</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Audio_Video_Interleave" title="Audio Video Interleave">AVI</a> – container (a shell, which enables any form of compression to be used)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bink_Video" title="Bink Video">BIK</a> (.bik) – Bink Video file. A video compression system developed by RAD Game Tools</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=CAM_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="CAM (file format) (page does not exist)">CAM</a> – <a href="/wiki/AMSN" title="AMSN">aMSN</a> webcam log file</li>
<li>COLLAB – Blackboard Collaborate session recording</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Digital_Audio_Tape" title="Digital Audio Tape">DAT</a> – video standard data file (automatically created when we attempted to burn as video file on the CD)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=DSH_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="DSH (file format) (page does not exist)">DSH</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DVR-MS" title="DVR-MS">DVR-MS</a> – <a href="/wiki/Windows_XP_Media_Center_Edition" title="Windows XP Media Center Edition">Windows XP Media Center Edition</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Windows_Media_Center" title="Windows Media Center">Windows Media Center</a> recorded television format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Flash_Video" title="Flash Video">FLV</a> – Flash video (encoded to run in a flash animation)</li>
<li>M1V <a href="/wiki/MPEG-1" title="MPEG-1">MPEG-1</a> – Video</li>
<li>M2V <a href="/wiki/MPEG-2" title="MPEG-2">MPEG-2</a> – Video</li>
<li>FLA – <a href="/wiki/Macromedia_Flash" class="mw-redirect" title="Macromedia Flash">Macromedia Flash</a> (for producing)</li>
<li>FLR – (text file which contains scripts extracted from SWF by a free ActionScript decompiler named <a href="/wiki/FLARE" class="mw-redirect" title="FLARE">FLARE</a>)</li>
<li>SOL – <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash" title="Adobe Flash">Adobe Flash</a> shared object ("<a href="/wiki/Flash_cookie" class="mw-redirect" title="Flash cookie">Flash cookie</a>")</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/M4V" title="M4V">M4V</a> – video container file format developed by <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Matroska" title="Matroska">Matroska</a> (*.mkv) – Matroska is a container format, which enables any video format such as <a href="/wiki/MPEG-4_Part_2" title="MPEG-4 Part 2">MPEG-4 ASP</a> or <a href="/wiki/H.264/MPEG-4_AVC" class="mw-redirect" title="H.264/MPEG-4 AVC">AVC</a> to be used along with other content such as <a href="/wiki/Subtitle_(captioning)" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtitle (captioning)">subtitles</a> and detailed <a href="/wiki/Metadata" title="Metadata">meta</a> information</li>
<li>WRAP – <a href="/w/index.php?title=MediaForge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="MediaForge (page does not exist)">MediaForge</a> (*.wrap)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Multiple-image_Network_Graphics" title="Multiple-image Network Graphics">MNG</a> – mainly simple animation containing PNG and JPEG objects, often somewhat more complex than animated GIF</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/QuickTime#File_formats" title="QuickTime">QuickTime</a> (.mov) – container which enables any form of compression to be used; <a href="/wiki/Sorenson_codec" class="mw-redirect" title="Sorenson codec">Sorenson codec</a> is the most common; <a href="/wiki/QTCH" class="mw-redirect" title="QTCH">QTCH</a> is the filetype for cached video and audio streams</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MPEG" class="mw-redirect" title="MPEG">MPEG</a> (.mpeg, .mpg, .mpe)</li>
<li>THP – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> proprietary movie/video format</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li><a href="/wiki/MPEG-4_Part_14" title="MPEG-4 Part 14">MPEG-4 Part 14</a>, shortened "<a href="/wiki/MP4" class="mw-redirect" title="MP4">MP4</a>" – multimedia container (most often used for Sony's <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable" title="PlayStation Portable">PlayStation Portable</a> and Apple's <a href="/wiki/IPod" title="IPod">iPod</a>)</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/MXF" class="mw-redirect" title="MXF">MXF</a> – Material Exchange Format (standardized wrapper format for audio/visual material developed by <a href="/wiki/SMPTE" class="mw-redirect" title="SMPTE">SMPTE</a>)</li>
<li>ROQ – used by <a href="/wiki/Quake_3" class="mw-redirect" title="Quake 3">Quake 3</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nullsoft_Streaming_Video" title="Nullsoft Streaming Video">NSV</a> – Nullsoft Streaming Video (media container designed for streaming video content over the Internet)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ogg" title="Ogg">Ogg</a> – container, multimedia</li>
<li>RM – <a href="/wiki/RealMedia" title="RealMedia">RealMedia</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=SVI_(file_format)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="SVI (file format) (page does not exist)">SVI</a> – Samsung video format for portable players</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SAMI" title="SAMI">SMI</a> – SAMI Caption file (HTML like subtitle for movie files)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Smacker_video" title="Smacker video">SMK</a> (.smk) – Smacker video file. A video compression system developed by RAD Game Tools</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SWF" title="SWF">SWF</a> – <a href="/wiki/Macromedia_Flash" class="mw-redirect" title="Macromedia Flash">Macromedia Flash</a> (for viewing)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Windows_Media_Video" title="Windows Media Video">WMV</a> – Windows Media Video (See ASF)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WTV_(Windows_Recorded_TV_Show)" title="WTV (Windows Recorded TV Show)">WTV</a> – <a href="/wiki/Windows_Vista" title="Windows Vista">Windows Vista</a>'s and up <a href="/wiki/Windows_Media_Center" title="Windows Media Center">Windows Media Center</a> recorded television format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/YUV" title="YUV">YUV</a> – raw video format; resolution (horizontal x vertical) and sample structure 4:2:2 or 4:2:0 must be known explicitly</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/WebM" title="WebM">WebM</a> – video file format for web video using HTML5</li></ul>
<h3><span id="Video_editing.2C_production"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_editing,_production">Video editing, production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Video editing, production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>BRAW – <a href="/wiki/Blackmagic_Design" title="Blackmagic Design">Blackmagic Design</a> RAW video file name</li>
<li>FCP – <a href="/wiki/Final_Cut_Pro" title="Final Cut Pro">Final Cut Pro</a> project file</li>
<li>MSWMM – <a href="/wiki/Windows_Movie_Maker" title="Windows Movie Maker">Windows Movie Maker</a> project file</li>
<li>PPJ &amp; PRPROJ– <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Premiere_Pro" title="Adobe Premiere Pro">Adobe Premiere Pro</a> video editing file</li>
<li>IMOVIEPROJ – <a href="/wiki/IMovie" title="IMovie">iMovie</a> project file</li>
<li>VEG &amp; VEG-BAK – Sony Vegas project file</li>
<li>SUF – Sony camera configuration file (setup.suf) produced by XDCAM-EX camcorders</li>
<li>WLMP – <a href="/wiki/Windows_Live_Movie_Maker" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows Live Movie Maker">Windows Live Movie Maker</a> project file</li>
<li>KDENLIVE – <a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kdenlive" class="extiw" title="fr:Kdenlive">Kdenlive</a> project file</li>
<li>VPJ – <a href="/wiki/VideoPad" class="mw-redirect" title="VideoPad">VideoPad</a> project file</li>
<li>MOTN – Apple <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.apple.com/final-cut-pro/motion/">Motion</a> project file</li>
<li>IMOVIEMOBILE – iMovie project file for <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> users</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_game_data">Video game data</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Video game data">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>List of common file formats of data for video games on systems that support filesystems, most commonly PC games.
</p>
<ul><li><b>TrackMania United/Nations Forever Engine</b> – Formats used by games based on the <a href="/wiki/TrackMania" title="TrackMania">TrackMania</a> engine.
<ul><li>XeX</li>
<li>CHALLENGE.GBX – (Edited) Challenge files.</li>
<li>CONSTRUCTIONCAMPAIGN.GBX – Construction campaigns files.</li>
<li>CONTROLEFFECTMASTER.GBX/CONTROLSTYLE.GBX – Menu parts.</li>
<li>FIDCACHE.GBX – Saved game.</li>
<li>GBX – Other TrackMania items.</li>
<li>REPLAY.GBX – Replays of races.</li></ul></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Doom_engine" title="Doom engine">Doom engine</a></b> – Formats used by games based on the <a href="/wiki/Doom_(video_game_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doom (video game series)">Doom</a> engine.
<ul><li>DEH – <a href="/wiki/DeHackEd" title="DeHackEd">DeHackEd</a> files to mutate the game executable (not officially part of the DOOM engine)</li>
<li>DSG – Saved game</li>
<li>LMP – A lump is an entry in a DOOM wad.</li>
<li>LMP – Saved demo recording</li>
<li>MUS – Music file (usually contained within a WAD file)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Doom_WAD" class="mw-redirect" title="Doom WAD">WAD</a> – Data storage (contains music, maps, and textures)</li></ul></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Quake_engine" title="Quake engine">Quake engine</a></b> – Formats used by games based on the <a href="/wiki/Quake_(series)" title="Quake (series)">Quake</a> engine.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/BSP_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="BSP (file format)">BSP</a> – (For <a href="/wiki/Binary_space_partitioning" title="Binary space partitioning">Binary space partitioning</a>) compiled map format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MAP_(file_format)" title="MAP (file format)">MAP</a> – Raw map format used by <a href="/wiki/Level_editor" class="mw-redirect" title="Level editor">editors</a> like <a href="/wiki/GtkRadiant" class="mw-redirect" title="GtkRadiant">GtkRadiant</a> or <a href="/wiki/Quake_Army_Knife" title="Quake Army Knife">QuArK</a></li>
<li>MDL/<a href="/wiki/MD2_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="MD2 (file format)">MD2</a>/<a href="/wiki/MD3_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="MD3 (file format)">MD3</a>/<a href="/wiki/MD5_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="MD5 (file format)">MD5</a> – Model for an item used in the game</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PAK_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="PAK (file format)">PAK</a>/<a href="/wiki/PK2_(file_extension)" title="PK2 (file extension)">PK2</a> – Data storage</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PK3_(file_extension)" class="mw-redirect" title="PK3 (file extension)">PK3</a>/<a href="/wiki/PK4_(file_extension)" class="mw-redirect" title="PK4 (file extension)">PK4</a> – used by the <a href="/wiki/Quake_II" title="Quake II">Quake II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quake_III_Arena" title="Quake III Arena">Quake III Arena</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quake_4" title="Quake 4">Quake 4</a> game engines, respectively, to store game data, textures etc. They are actually <a href="/wiki/.zip" class="mw-redirect" title=".zip">.zip</a> files.</li>
<li>.dat – not specific file type, often generic extension for "data" files for a variety of applications
<ul><li>sometimes used for general data contained within the .PK3/PK4 files</li>
<li>.fontdat – a .dat file used for formatting game fonts</li></ul></li>
<li>.roq – Video format</li>
<li>.sav – Savegame format</li></ul></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Unreal_Engine" title="Unreal Engine">Unreal Engine</a></b> – Formats used by games based on the <a href="/wiki/Unreal_(1998_video_game)" title="Unreal (1998 video game)">Unreal</a> engine.
<ul><li>U – Unreal script format</li>
<li>UAX – Animations format for Unreal Engine 2</li>
<li>UMX – Map format for <a href="/wiki/Unreal_Tournament" title="Unreal Tournament">Unreal Tournament</a></li>
<li>UMX – Music format for Unreal Engine 1</li>
<li>UNR – Map format for <a href="/wiki/Unreal_(1998_video_game)" title="Unreal (1998 video game)">Unreal</a></li>
<li>UPK – Package format for cooked content in Unreal Engine 3</li>
<li>USX – Sound format for Unreal Engine 1 and Unreal Engine 2</li>
<li>UT2 – Map format for <a href="/wiki/Unreal_Tournament_2003" title="Unreal Tournament 2003">Unreal Tournament 2003</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unreal_Tournament_2004" title="Unreal Tournament 2004">Unreal Tournament 2004</a></li>
<li>UT3 – Map format for <a href="/wiki/Unreal_Tournament_3" title="Unreal Tournament 3">Unreal Tournament 3</a></li>
<li>UTX – Texture format for Unreal Engine 1 and Unreal Engine 2</li>
<li>UXX – Cache format; these are files a client downloaded from server (which can be converted to regular formats)</li></ul></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Duke_Nukem_3D" title="Duke Nukem 3D">Duke Nukem 3D</a> Engine</b> – Formats used by games based on this engine
<ul><li>DMO – Save game</li>
<li>GRP – Data storage</li>
<li>MAP – Map (usually constructed with <a href="/wiki/Build_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Build engine">BUILD.EXE</a>)</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Diablo Engine</b> – Formats used by Diablo by Blizzard Entertainment.
<ul><li>SV – Save Game</li>
<li>ITM – Item File</li></ul></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Real_Virtuality_(engine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Real Virtuality (engine)">Real Virtuality</a> Engine</b> – Formats used by <a href="/wiki/Bohemia_Interactive" title="Bohemia Interactive">Bohemia Interactive</a>. <a href="/wiki/Operation:Flashpoint" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation:Flashpoint">Operation:Flashpoint</a>, <a href="/wiki/ARMA_2" title="ARMA 2">ARMA 2</a>, VBS2
<ul><li>SQF – Format used for general editing</li>
<li>SQM – Format used for mission files</li>
<li>PBO – Binarized file used for compiled models</li>
<li>LIP – Format that is created from WAV files to create in-game accurate lip-synch for character animations.</li></ul></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Source_(game_engine)" title="Source (game engine)">Source</a> Engine</b> – Formats used by <a href="/wiki/Valve_Corporation" title="Valve Corporation">Valve</a>. <a href="/wiki/Half-Life_2" title="Half-Life 2">Half-Life 2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Counter-Strike:_Source" title="Counter-Strike: Source">Counter-Strike: Source</a>, <a href="/wiki/Day_of_Defeat:_Source" title="Day of Defeat: Source">Day of Defeat: Source</a>, <a href="/wiki/Half-Life_2:_Episode_One" title="Half-Life 2: Episode One">Half-Life 2: Episode One</a>, <a href="/wiki/Team_Fortress_2" title="Team Fortress 2">Team Fortress 2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Half-Life_2:_Episode_Two" title="Half-Life 2: Episode Two">Half-Life 2: Episode Two</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portal_(video_game)" title="Portal (video game)">Portal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Left_4_Dead" title="Left 4 Dead">Left 4 Dead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Left_4_Dead_2" title="Left 4 Dead 2">Left 4 Dead 2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alien_Swarm" title="Alien Swarm">Alien Swarm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portal_2" title="Portal 2">Portal 2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Counter-Strike:_Global_Offensive" title="Counter-Strike: Global Offensive">Counter-Strike: Global Offensive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Titanfall" title="Titanfall">Titanfall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Insurgency" title="Insurgency">Insurgency</a>, <a href="/wiki/Titanfall_2" title="Titanfall 2">Titanfall 2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Day_of_Infamy" class="mw-redirect" title="Day of Infamy">Day of Infamy</a>
<ul><li>VMF – Valve Hammer Map editor raw map file</li>
<li>BSP – Source Engine compiled map file</li>
<li>MDL – Source Engine model format</li>
<li>SMD – Source Engine uncompiled model format</li>
<li>PCF – Source Engine particle effect file</li>
<li>HL2 – Half-Life 2 save format</li>
<li>DEM – Source Engine demo format</li>
<li>VPK – Source Engine pack format</li>
<li>VTF – Source Engine texture format</li>
<li>VMT – Source Engine material format.</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Other Formats</b>
<ul><li>B – used for <a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_(Video_Game)" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Theft Auto (Video Game)">Grand Theft Auto</a> saved game files</li>
<li>BOL – used for levels on Poing!PC</li>
<li>DBPF – <a href="/wiki/The_Sims_2" title="The Sims 2">The Sims 2</a>, DBPF, Package</li>
<li>DIVA – <a href="/wiki/Project_DIVA" class="mw-redirect" title="Project DIVA">Project DIVA</a> timings, <a href="/wiki/Element_(UML)" title="Element (UML)">element</a> coördinates, MP3 references, notes, <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">animation poses</a> and scores.</li>
<li>ESM, ESP – Master and Plugin data archives for the <a href="/wiki/Creation_Engine" title="Creation Engine">Creation Engine</a></li>
<li>HE0, HE2, HE4 HE games File</li>
<li>GCF – format used by the <a href="/wiki/Steam_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Steam (software)">Steam</a> content management system for file archives</li>
<li>IMG – format used by <a href="/wiki/Renderware" class="mw-redirect" title="Renderware">Renderware</a>-based <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto" title="Grand Theft Auto">Grand Theft Auto</a></i> games for data storage</li>
<li>LOVE – format used by the LOVE2D Engine<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>MAP – format used by <a href="/wiki/Halo:_Combat_Evolved" title="Halo: Combat Evolved">Halo: Combat Evolved</a> for archive compression, Doom³, and various other games</li>
<li>MCA – format used by <a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a> for storing data for in-game worlds<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>MCADDON – format used by the Windows 10 Edition of <a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a> for add-ons</li>
<li>MCFUNCTION – format used by <a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a> for storing functions</li>
<li>MCMETA – format used by <a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a> for storing data for customizable texture packs for the game</li>
<li>MCPACK – format used by the Windows 10 Edition of <a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a> for in-game texture packs</li>
<li>MCR – format used by <a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a> for storing data for in-game worlds before version 1.2</li>
<li>MCTEMPLATE – format used by the Windows 10 Edition of <a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a> for world templates</li>
<li>MCWORLD – format used by the Windows 10 Edition of <a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a> for in-game worlds</li>
<li>NBT – format used by <a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a> for storing program variables along with their (Java) type identifiers</li>
<li>OEC – format used by <a href="/wiki/OE-Cake" class="mw-redirect" title="OE-Cake">OE-Cake</a> for scene data storage</li>
<li>OSK – <a href="/wiki/Osu!" title="Osu!">osu!</a> compressed skin data</li>
<li>OSR – <a href="/wiki/Osu!" title="Osu!">osu!</a> replay data</li>
<li>OSU – <a href="/wiki/Osu!" title="Osu!">osu!</a> beatmap data</li>
<li>P3D – format for panda3d by Disney</li>
<li>POD – format used by <a href="/wiki/Terminal_Reality" title="Terminal Reality">Terminal Reality</a></li>
<li>RCT – Used for templates and save files in <a href="/wiki/RollerCoaster_Tycoon" title="RollerCoaster Tycoon">RollerCoaster Tycoon</a> games</li>
<li>REP – used by <a href="/wiki/Blizzard_Entertainment" title="Blizzard Entertainment">Blizzard Entertainment</a> for scenario replays in <a href="/wiki/StarCraft" title="StarCraft">StarCraft</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Simcity_4" class="mw-redirect" title="Simcity 4">Simcity 4</a>, DBPF (.dat, .SC4Lot, .SC4Model) – All game plugins use this format, commonly with different file extensions</li>
<li>SMZIP – ZIP-based package for <a href="/wiki/Stepmania" class="mw-redirect" title="Stepmania">Stepmania</a> songs, themes and announcer packs.</li>
<li>USLD – format used by Unison Shift to store level layouts.</li>
<li>VVVVVV – format used by <a href="/wiki/VVVVVV" title="VVVVVV">VVVVVV</a><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>CPS – format used by <a href="/wiki/The_Powder_Toy" title="The Powder Toy">The Powder Toy</a>, Powder Toy save</li>
<li>STM – format used by <a href="/wiki/The_Powder_Toy" title="The Powder Toy">The Powder Toy</a>, Powder Toy stamp</li>
<li>PKG – format used by <a href="/wiki/Bungie" title="Bungie">Bungie</a> for the PC Beta of <a href="/wiki/Destiny_2" title="Destiny 2">Destiny 2</a>, for nearly all the game's assets.</li>
<li>CHR – format used by <a href="/wiki/Team_Salvato" class="mw-redirect" title="Team Salvato">Team Salvato</a>, for the character files of <a href="/wiki/Doki_Doki_Literature_Club!" title="Doki Doki Literature Club!">Doki Doki Literature Club!</a></li>
<li>Z5 – format used by <a href="/wiki/Z-machine" title="Z-machine">Z-machine</a> for story files in interactive fiction.</li>
<li>scworld – format used by <a href="/wiki/Survivalcraft" title="Survivalcraft">Survivalcraft</a> to store sandbox worlds.</li>
<li>scskin – format used by <a href="/wiki/Survivalcraft" title="Survivalcraft">Survivalcraft</a> to store player skins.</li>
<li>scbtex – format used by <a href="/wiki/Survivalcraft" title="Survivalcraft">Survivalcraft</a> to store block textures.</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_game_storage_media">Video game storage media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: Video game storage media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>List of the most common filename extensions used when a game's <a href="/wiki/ROM_image" title="ROM image">ROM image</a> or storage medium is copied from an original <a href="/wiki/Read-only_memory" title="Read-only memory">read-only memory</a> (ROM) device to an external memory such as <a href="/wiki/Hard_disk" class="mw-redirect" title="Hard disk">hard disk</a> for <a href="/wiki/Back_up" class="mw-redirect" title="Back up">back up</a> purposes or for making the game playable with an <a href="/wiki/Emulator" title="Emulator">emulator</a>. In the case of cartridge-based software, if the platform specific extension is not used then filename extensions ".rom" or ".bin" are usually used to clarify that the file contains a copy of a content of a ROM. ROM, disk or tape images usually do not consist of one file or ROM, rather an entire file or ROM structure contained within one file on the backup medium.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>A26 – <a href="/wiki/Atari_2600" title="Atari 2600">Atari 2600</a> (.a26)</li>
<li>A52 – <a href="/wiki/Atari_5200" title="Atari 5200">Atari 5200</a> (.a52)</li>
<li>A78 – <a href="/wiki/Atari_7800" title="Atari 7800">Atari 7800</a> (.a78)</li>
<li>LNX – <a href="/wiki/Atari_Lynx" title="Atari Lynx">Atari Lynx</a> (.lnx)</li>
<li>JAG,J64 – <a href="/wiki/Atari_Jaguar" title="Atari Jaguar">Atari Jaguar</a> (.jag, .j64)</li>
<li>ISO, WBFS, WAD, WDF – <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> (.iso, .wbfs, .wad, .wdf)</li>
<li>GCM, ISO – <a href="/wiki/GameCube" title="GameCube">GameCube</a> (.gcm, .iso)</li>
<li>NDS – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a> (.nds)</li>
<li>3DS – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_3DS" title="Nintendo 3DS">Nintendo 3DS</a> (.3ds)</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>CIA – Installation File (.cia)</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>GB – <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy" title="Game Boy">Game Boy</a> (.gb) (this applies to the original Game Boy and the <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy_Color" title="Game Boy Color">Game Boy Color</a>)</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>GBC – <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy_Color" title="Game Boy Color">Game Boy Color</a> (.gbc)</li>
<li>GBA – <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy_Advance" title="Game Boy Advance">Game Boy Advance</a> (.gba)</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>GBA – <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy_Advance" title="Game Boy Advance">Game Boy Advance</a> (.gba)</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>SAV – <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy_Advance" title="Game Boy Advance">Game Boy Advance</a> Saved Data Files (.sav)</li>
<li>SGM – <a href="/wiki/Visual_Boy_Advance" class="mw-redirect" title="Visual Boy Advance">Visual Boy Advance</a> Save States (.sgm)</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>N64, V64, Z64, U64, USA, JAP, PAL, EUR, BIN – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_64" title="Nintendo 64">Nintendo 64</a> (.n64, .v64, .z64, .u64, .usa, .jap, .pal, .eur, .bin)</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>PJ – <a href="/wiki/Project64" title="Project64">Project 64</a> Save States (.pj)</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>NES – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_Entertainment_System" title="Nintendo Entertainment System">Nintendo Entertainment System</a> (.nes)</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>FDS – <a href="/wiki/Family_Computer_Disk_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Family Computer Disk System">Famicom Disk System</a> (.fds)</li>
<li>JST – Jnes Save States (.jst)</li>
<li>FC? – <a href="/wiki/FCEUX" title="FCEUX">FCEUX</a> Save States (.fc#, where # is any character, usually a number)</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>GG – <a href="/wiki/Game_Gear" title="Game Gear">Game Gear</a> (.gg)</li>
<li>SMS – <a href="/wiki/Master_System" title="Master System">Master System</a> (.sms)</li>
<li>SG – <a href="/wiki/SG-1000" title="SG-1000">SG-1000</a> (.sg)</li>
<li>SMD,BIN – <a href="/wiki/Sega_Genesis" title="Sega Genesis">Mega Drive/Genesis</a> (.smd or .bin)</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>32X – <a href="/wiki/32X" title="32X">Sega 32X</a> (.32x)</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>SMC,078,SFC – <a href="/wiki/Super_Nintendo_Entertainment_System" title="Super Nintendo Entertainment System">Super NES</a> (.smc, .078, or .sfc) (.078 is for split ROMs, which are rare)</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>FIG – Super Famicom (Japanese releases are rarely .fig, above extensions are more common)</li>
<li>SRM – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Super_NES_Saved_Data_Files&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Super NES Saved Data Files (page does not exist)">Super NES Saved Data Files</a> (.srm)</li>
<li>ZST – <a href="/wiki/ZSNES" title="ZSNES">ZSNES</a> Save States (.zst, .zs1-.zs9, .z10-.z99)</li>
<li>FRZ – <a href="/wiki/Snes9X" class="mw-redirect" title="Snes9X">Snes9X</a> Save States (.frz, .000-.008)</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>PCE – <a href="/wiki/TurboGrafx_16" class="mw-redirect" title="TurboGrafx 16">TurboGrafx-16/PC Engine</a> (.pce)</li>
<li>NPC, NGP – <a href="/wiki/Neo_Geo_Pocket" title="Neo Geo Pocket">Neo Geo Pocket</a> (.npc, .ngp)</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>NGC – <a href="/wiki/Neo_Geo_Pocket_Color" title="Neo Geo Pocket Color">Neo Geo Pocket Color</a> (.ngc)</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>VB  – <a href="/wiki/Virtual_Boy" title="Virtual Boy">Virtual Boy</a> (.vb)</li>
<li>INT – <a href="/wiki/Intellivision" title="Intellivision">Intellivision</a> (.int)</li>
<li>MIN – <a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_Mini" title="Pokémon Mini">Pokémon Mini</a> (.min)</li>
<li>VEC – <a href="/wiki/Vectrex" title="Vectrex">Vectrex</a> (.vec)</li>
<li>BIN – <a href="/wiki/Magnavox_Odyssey%C2%B2" title="Magnavox Odyssey²">Odyssey²</a> (.bin)</li>
<li>WS – <a href="/wiki/WonderSwan" title="WonderSwan">WonderSwan</a> (.ws)</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>WSC – <a href="/wiki/WonderSwan" title="WonderSwan">WonderSwan Color</a> (.wsc)</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>TZX – <a href="/wiki/ZX_Spectrum" title="ZX Spectrum">ZX Spectrum</a> (.tzx) (for exact copies of ZX Spectrum games)</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>TAP – for tape images without copy protection</li>
<li>Z80,SNA – (for snapshots of the emulator RAM)</li>
<li>DSK – (for disk images)</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>TAP – <a href="/wiki/Commodore_64" title="Commodore 64">Commodore 64</a> (.tap) (for tape images including copy protection)</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>T64 – (for tape images without copy protection, considerably smaller than .tap files)</li>
<li>D64 – (for disk images)</li>
<li>CRT – (for cartridge images)</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>ADF – <a href="/wiki/Amiga" title="Amiga">Amiga</a> (.adf) (for 880K diskette images)</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li>ADZ – <a href="/wiki/GZip" class="mw-redirect" title="GZip">GZip</a>-compressed version of the above.</li>
<li>DMS – <i>Disk Masher System</i>, previously used as a disk-archiving system native to the Amiga, also supported by emulators.</li></ul></dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Virtual_machines"><a href="/wiki/Virtual_machines" class="mw-redirect" title="Virtual machines">Virtual machines</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Virtual machines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Microsoft_Virtual_PC.2C_Virtual_Server"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Microsoft_Virtual_PC,_Virtual_Server"><a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Virtual_PC" class="mw-redirect" title="Microsoft Virtual PC">Microsoft Virtual PC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Virtual_Server" title="Microsoft Virtual Server">Virtual Server</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Microsoft Virtual PC, Virtual Server">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>VFD – Virtual Floppy Disk (.vfd)</li>
<li>VHD – Virtual Hard Disk (.vhd)</li>
<li>VUD – Virtual Undo Disk (.vud)</li>
<li>VMC – Virtual Machine Configuration (.vmc)</li>
<li>VSV – Virtual Machine Saved State (.vsv)</li></ul>
<h3><span id="EMC_VMware_ESX.2C_GSX.2C_Workstation.2C_Player"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="EMC_VMware_ESX,_GSX,_Workstation,_Player">EMC <a href="/wiki/VMware" title="VMware">VMware</a> ESX, GSX, <a href="/wiki/VMware_Workstation" title="VMware Workstation">Workstation</a>, <a href="/wiki/VMware_Player" class="mw-redirect" title="VMware Player">Player</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: EMC VMware ESX, GSX, Workstation, Player">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>LOG – Virtual Machine Logfile (.log)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/VMDK" title="VMDK">VMDK</a>, DSK – Virtual Machine Disk (.vmdk, .dsk)</li>
<li>NVRAM – Virtual Machine BIOS (.nvram)</li>
<li>VMEM – Virtual Machine paging file (.vmem)</li>
<li>VMSD – Virtual Machine snapshot metadata (.vmsd)</li>
<li>VMSN – Virtual Machine snapshot (.vmsn)</li>
<li>VMSS,STD – Virtual Machine suspended state (.vmss, .std)</li>
<li>VMTM – Virtual Machine team data (.vmtm)</li>
<li>VMX,CFG – Virtual Machine configuration (.vmx, .cfg)</li>
<li>VMXF – Virtual Machine team configuration (.vmxf)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="VirtualBox"><a href="/wiki/VirtualBox" title="VirtualBox">VirtualBox</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: VirtualBox">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>VDI – VirtualBox Virtual Disk Image (.vdi)</li>
<li>Vbox-extpack – VitualBox extension pack. (.vbox-extpack)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parallels_Workstation">Parallels Workstation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=69" title="Edit section: Parallels Workstation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parallels_Workstation" title="Parallels Workstation">Parallels Workstation</a></div>
<ul><li>HDD – Virtual Machine hard disk (.hdd)</li>
<li>PVS – Virtual Machine preferences/configuration (.pvs)</li>
<li>SAV – Virtual Machine saved state (.sav)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="QEMU"><a href="/wiki/QEMU" title="QEMU">QEMU</a></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: QEMU">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>COW – <a href="/wiki/Copy-on-write" title="Copy-on-write">Copy-on-write</a></li>
<li>QCOW – QEMU copy-on-write <a href="/wiki/Qcow" title="Qcow">Qcow</a></li>
<li>QCOW2 – QEMU copy-on-write – version 2 <a href="/wiki/Qcow" title="Qcow">Qcow</a></li>
<li>QED – QEMU enhanced disk format</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Web_page">Web page</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=71" title="Edit section: Web page">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Static_code_analysis" class="mw-redirect" title="Static code analysis">Static</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Document_Type_Definition" class="mw-redirect" title="Document Type Definition">DTD</a> – Document Type Definition (standard), MUST be public and free</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> (.html, .htm) – HyperText Markup Language</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a> (.xhtml, .xht) – eXtensible HyperText Markup Language</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MHTML" title="MHTML">MHTML</a> (.mht, .mhtml) – Archived HTML, store all data on one web page (text, images, etc.) in one big file</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Archive_Format" title="Mozilla Archive Format">MAF</a> (.maff) – web archive based on <a href="/wiki/ZIP_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="ZIP (file format)">ZIP</a></li></ul></li>
<li>Dynamically generated
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Active_Server_Pages" title="Active Server Pages">ASP</a> (.asp) – Microsoft Active Server Page</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ASP.NET" title="ASP.NET">ASPX</a> – (.aspx) – Microsoft Active Server Page. NET</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AOLserver" title="AOLserver">ADP</a> – AOLserver Dynamic Page</li>
<li>BML – (.bml) – Better Markup Language (templating)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ColdFusion" class="mw-redirect" title="ColdFusion">CFM</a> – (.cfm) – ColdFusion</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Common_Gateway_Interface" title="Common Gateway Interface">CGI</a> – (.cgi)</li>
<li>iHTML – (.ihtml) – Inline HTML</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JavaServer_Pages" title="JavaServer Pages">JSP</a> – (.jsp) JavaServer Pages</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lasso_(programming_language)" title="Lasso (programming language)">Lasso</a> – (.las, .lasso, .lassoapp) – A file created or served with the Lasso Programming Language</li>
<li>PL – <a href="/wiki/Perl" title="Perl">Perl</a> (.pl)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">PHP</a> – (.php, .php?, .phtml) –&#160;? is version number (previously abbreviated <i>Personal Home Page</i>, later changed to <i>PHP: Hypertext Preprocessor</i>)</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.socialgeek.eu/help/rnaformat?">RNA</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title="&#160;Dead link since December 2017">permanent dead link</span></a></i>&#93;</span></sup> – (.rna) – Real Native Application File</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.socialgeek.eu/help/rnaformat?">R</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title="&#160;Dead link since December 2017">permanent dead link</span></a></i>&#93;</span></sup> – (.r) – Real Native Application File (short alternative)</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.socialgeek.eu/help/rnaformat?">RNX</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title="&#160;Dead link since December 2017">permanent dead link</span></a></i>&#93;</span></sup> – (.rnx) – Real Native Application File (using experimental version 6 of RNA/Karbon Language)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Server_Side_Includes" title="Server Side Includes">SSI</a> – (.shtml) – HTML with Server Side Includes (Apache)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Server_Side_Includes" title="Server Side Includes">SSI</a> – (.stm) – HTML with Server Side Includes (Apache)</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Markup_languages_and_other_web_standards-based_formats">Markup languages and other web standards-based formats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=72" title="Edit section: Markup languages and other web standards-based formats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Atom_(standard)" class="mw-redirect" title="Atom (standard)">Atom</a> – (.atom, .xml) – Another syndication format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Email#Filename_extensions" title="Email">EML</a> – (.eml) – Format used by several desktop email clients</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JSON-LD" title="JSON-LD">JSON-LD</a> – (.jsonld) – A JSON-based Serialization for Linked Data</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Metalink" title="Metalink">Metalink</a> – (.metalink, .met) – A format to list metadata about downloads, such as mirrors, checksums, and other information.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/RSS_(file_format)" class="mw-redirect" title="RSS (file format)">RSS</a> – (.rss, .xml) – Syndication format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Markdown" title="Markdown">Markdown</a> – (.markdown, .md) – A light-weight, plain-text, easy to read and write markup language.</li>
<li>Shuttle – (.se) – lightweight markup language</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=73" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>AXD – cookie extensions found in temporary internet folder</li>
<li>BDF – Binary Data Format – raw data from recovered blocks of unallocated space on a hard drive</li>
<li>CBP – CD Box Labeler Pro, CentraBuilder, Code::Blocks Project File, Conlab Project<sup id="cite_ref-filext-cbp_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filext-cbp-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>CEX – SolidWorks Enterprise PDM Vault File</li>
<li>COL – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> <a href="/wiki/GameCube" title="GameCube">GameCube</a> proprietary collision file (.col)</li>
<li>CREDX – CredX Dat File</li>
<li>DDB – Generating code for <a href="/wiki/Vocaloid" title="Vocaloid">Vocaloid</a> singers voice (see .DDI)</li>
<li>DDI – <a href="/wiki/Vocaloid" title="Vocaloid">Vocaloid</a> <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phoneme</a> library (Japanese, English, Korean, Spanish, Chinese, Catalan)</li>
<li>DUPX – DuupeCheck database management tool project file</li>
<li>FTM – Family Tree Maker data file</li>
<li>FTMB – Family Tree Maker backup file</li>
<li>GA3 – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Graphical_Analysis_3&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Graphical Analysis 3 (page does not exist)">Graphical Analysis 3</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GEDCOM" title="GEDCOM">GEDCOM</a> (.ged) – (GEnealogical Data COMmunication) format to exchange <a href="/wiki/Genealogy" title="Genealogy">genealogy</a> <a href="/wiki/Data" title="Data">data</a> between different <a href="/wiki/Genealogy_software" title="Genealogy software">genealogy software</a></li>
<li>HLP – Windows help file</li>
<li>IGC – flight tracks downloaded from GPS devices in the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_A%C3%A9ronautique_Internationale" title="Fédération Aéronautique Internationale">FAI's</a> prescribed format</li>
<li>INF – similar format to <a href="/wiki/INI_file" title="INI file">INI file</a>; used to install device drivers under Windows, inter alia.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JAM_Message_Base_Format" title="JAM Message Base Format">JAM</a> – JAM Message Base Format for BBSes</li>
<li>KMC – tests made with KatzReview's MegaCrammer</li>
<li>KCL – <a href="/wiki/Nintendo" title="Nintendo">Nintendo</a> <a href="/wiki/GameCube" title="GameCube">GameCube</a>/<a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a> proprietary collision file (.kcl)</li>
<li>LNK – <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> <a href="/wiki/Windows" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows">Windows</a> format for <a href="/wiki/Hyperlinks" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyperlinks">Hyperlinks</a> to <a href="/wiki/Executable" title="Executable">Executables</a></li>
<li>LSM – LSMaker script file (program using layered .jpg to create special effects; specifically designed to render <a href="/wiki/Lightsaber" title="Lightsaber">lightsabers</a> from the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> universe) (.lsm)</li>
<li>NARC – Archive format used in <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a> games.</li>
<li>OER – AU OER Tool, Open Educational Resource editor</li>
<li>PA – Used to assign sound effects to materials in KCL files (.pa)</li>
<li>PIF – Used to run <a href="/wiki/MS-DOS" title="MS-DOS">MS-DOS</a> programs under Windows</li>
<li>POR – So called "portable" SPSS files, readable by <a href="/wiki/PSPP" title="PSPP">PSPP</a></li>
<li>PXZ – Compressed file to exchange media elements with PSALMO</li>
<li>RISE – File containing RISE generated information model evolution</li>
<li>TOPC – TopicCrunch SEO Project file holding keywords, domain and search engine settings (ASCII);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/.tos" class="mw-redirect" title=".tos">TOS</a> – Character file from <a href="/wiki/The_Only_Sheet" title="The Only Sheet">The Only Sheet</a></li>
<li>XLF – <a href="/wiki/Utah_State_University" title="Utah State University">Utah State University</a> Extensible LADAR Format</li>
<li>XMC – Assisted contact lists format, based on XML and used in kindergartens and schools</li>
<li>ZED – My Heritage Family Tree</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zone_file" title="Zone file">Zone file</a> – a <a href="/wiki/Text_file" title="Text file">text file</a> containing a <a href="/wiki/DNS_zone" title="DNS zone">DNS zone</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cursors">Cursors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=74" title="Edit section: Cursors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/ANI_(file_format)" title="ANI (file format)">ANI</a> – Animated cursor</li>
<li>CUR – Cursor file</li>
<li>Smes – Hawk's Dock configuration file</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Generalized_files">Generalized files</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: Generalized files">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General_data_formats">General data formats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: General data formats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>These file formats are fairly well defined by long-term use or a general standard, but the content of each file is often highly specific to particular software or has been extended by further standards for specific uses.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Text-based">Text-based</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Text-based">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>CSV – <a href="/wiki/Comma-separated_values" title="Comma-separated values">comma-separated values</a></li>
<li>HTML – <a href="/wiki/Hyper_text_markup_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyper text markup language">hyper text markup language</a></li>
<li>CSS – <a href="/wiki/Cascading_style_sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading style sheets">cascading style sheets</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/INI_file" title="INI file">INI</a> – a configuration text file whose format is substantially similar between applications</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/JSON" title="JSON">JSON</a> – JavaScript Object Notation is an openly used data format now used by many languages, not just JavaScript</li>
<li>TSV – <a href="/wiki/Tab-separated_values" title="Tab-separated values">tab-separated values</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> – an open data format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/YAML" title="YAML">YAML</a> – an open data format</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/ReStructuredText" title="ReStructuredText">ReStructuredText</a> – an open text format for technical documents used mainly in the <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a> programming language</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Markdown" title="Markdown">Markdown</a> (.md) – an open lightweight markup language to create simple but rich text, often used to format <a href="/wiki/README" title="README">README</a> files</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AsciiDoc" title="AsciiDoc">AsciiDoc</a> – an open human-readable markup document format semantically equivalent to <a href="/wiki/DocBook" title="DocBook">DocBook</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Generic_file_extensions">Generic file extensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: Generic file extensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>These are filename extensions and broad types reused frequently with differing formats or no specific format by different programs.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Binary_files">Binary files</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=79" title="Edit section: Binary files">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bak_file" title="Bak file">Bak file</a> (.bak, .bk) – various backup formats: some just copies of data files, some in application-specific data backup formats, some formats for general file backup programs</li>
<li>BIN – binary data, often <a href="/wiki/Memory_dump" class="mw-redirect" title="Memory dump">memory dumps</a> of executable code or data to be re-used by the same software that originated it</li>
<li>DAT – data file, usually binary data proprietary to the program that created it</li>
<li>DSK – file representations of various <a href="/wiki/Disk_storage" title="Disk storage">disk storage</a> images</li>
<li>RAW – raw (unprocessed) data</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Text_files">Text files</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=80" title="Edit section: Text files">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Configuration_file" title="Configuration file">configuration file</a> (.cnf, .conf, .cfg) – substantially software-specific</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Logfile" class="mw-redirect" title="Logfile">logfiles</a> (.log) – usually text, but sometimes binary</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Plain_text" title="Plain text">plain text</a> (.asc or .txt) – human-readable <a href="/wiki/Plain_text" title="Plain text">plain text</a>, usually no more specific</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Partial_files">Partial files</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=81" title="Edit section: Partial files">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Differences_and_patches">Differences and patches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=82" title="Edit section: Differences and patches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Diff" title="Diff">diff</a> – text file differences created by the program <a href="/wiki/Diff" title="Diff">diff</a> and applied as updates by <a href="/wiki/Patch_(Unix)" title="Patch (Unix)">patch</a></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Incomplete_transfers">Incomplete transfers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=83" title="Edit section: Incomplete transfers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li>!UT (.!ut) – partly complete <a href="/wiki/UTorrent" class="mw-redirect" title="UTorrent">uTorrent</a> download</li>
<li>CRDOWNLOAD (.crdownload) – partly complete <a href="/wiki/Google_Chrome" title="Google Chrome">Google Chrome</a> download</li>
<li>OPDOWNLOAD (.opdownload) – partly complete <a href="/wiki/Opera_(web_browser)" title="Opera (web browser)">Opera</a> download</li>
<li>PART (.part) – partly complete <a href="/wiki/Mozilla_Firefox" class="mw-redirect" title="Mozilla Firefox">Mozilla Firefox</a> or <a href="/wiki/Transmission_(BitTorrent_client)" title="Transmission (BitTorrent client)">Transmission</a> download</li>
<li>PARTIAL (.partial) – partly complete <a href="/wiki/Internet_Explorer" title="Internet Explorer">Internet Explorer</a> or <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Edge" title="Microsoft Edge">Microsoft Edge</a> download</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Temporary_files">Temporary files</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=84" title="Edit section: Temporary files">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Temporary_file" title="Temporary file">Temporary file</a> (.temp, .tmp, various others) – sometimes in a specific format, but often just raw data in the middle of processing
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pipeline_(software)#Pseudo-pipelines" title="Pipeline (software)">Pseudo-pipeline</a> file – used to simulate a software pipe</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_file_formats&amp;action=edit&amp;section=85" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_filename_extensions" title="List of filename extensions">List of filename extensions</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/MIME#Content-Type" title="MIME">MIME#Content-Type</a>, a standard for referring to file formats</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_motion_and_gesture_file_formats" title="List of motion and gesture file formats">List of motion and gesture file formats</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_file_signatures" title="List of file signatures">List of file signatures</a>, or "magic numbers"</li></ul>
